US Senate Passes Philippine Independence Bill 66

Twelve Years as a Trial Period, First Granted Autonomous Status

Expected that the President May Not Approve

Reuters, Washington, December 17th - The United States Senate has been debating the Philippine independence issue for several days. Today, it passed an amendment that would grant the Philippines independence within twelve years. Previously, it had been proposed that the Philippines be granted independence after eighteen years, and later someone suggested changing eighteen years to eight years. Therefore, today's amendment is a compromise solution.

National News Agency, Washington, December 17th - Today, the U.S. Senate, with unexpected speed, passed the Hare-Hawes-Cutting Philippine Independence Act by a large majority. It will immediately be transferred to a joint House-Senate conference committee to reconcile it with the Hare Act passed by the House in the previous session. After adjustments, it will be submitted to both houses for adoption. According to original proposer Hawes' guarantee, this bill can be put to a final vote in both houses before the Christmas holiday. The bill passed by the Senate today includes the Broussard Amendment, which stipulates that the Philippines be granted independence after twelve years. However, the Philippines must convene a constitutional convention within two years to draft a constitution. This constitution must be approved by the U.S. Congress and the U.S. President. From the date this bill is finally established until the U.S. approves its implementation of independence, the intervening period will be granted the status of an autonomous territory. Although Filipinos can have a more autonomous government, they will not be able to trade with the United States completely tax-free, nor will they be allowed to immigrate to Honolulu and the United States without restriction. The most obvious difference between this bill and the Hare Act is the length of the transition period. The Hare Act only stipulated eight years, but many in the Senate believe that this point is easy to compromise. Other provisions include asking the President to negotiate treaties with various countries to guarantee the Philippines' freedom, and restricting the import of Philippine goods and the immigration of Philippine workers. The differences are only minor details. However, even if this bill is passed by both houses, it is expected that President Hoover will veto it. But it is believed that both houses will still have sufficient votes to overturn Hoover's veto, because Hoover and Stimson, etc., all believe that Filipinos currently lack sufficient political training and should not lightly risk the dangers of autonomy. They also believe that the Philippines should not break away from American rule until its economy is independent. However, the Senate's passage of this bill is not purely based on ideals. Its main intention is to help American agriculture, the Cuban sugar industry, and American labor, in order to reduce Philippine competition. Therefore, both the Republican and Democratic parties currently have supporters of independence. So, once Philippine independence becomes a reality, the economic recession is indeed a major driving force behind it.

The Manchurian Problem and the League of Nations (5)

Verbal Sparring Between the Chinese and Japanese Representatives in the Commission of Enquiry

Japan cannot turn a blind eye to any disturbances in any part of East Asia, because the spirit of the Japanese Empire cannot coexist with disturbances. Every Japanese citizen should be prepared spiritually and materially at all times to restore stability, even resorting to force if necessary." This article by Araki embodies the spirit and scope of Japanese policy. As for its implementation methods, we can get a general idea by looking at the records of Mutsu Munemitsu, the Japanese Foreign Minister during the Sino-Japanese War of 1894-1895. Mutsu Munemitsu's position during the Sino-Japanese War was extremely important. The cause of the Sino-Japanese War has been a point of contention in general public opinion for decades. After the publication of Okuriku's records, the doubts began to subside, because Japan's responsibility for forcing China to fight became undeniable. Around June 1894, a large number of Japanese army and navy troops were dispatched to Korea, led by Keisuke Oshima, the Japanese ambassador to Korea. At that time, the situation in Korea was gradually stabilizing, and the plan to wage war against China seemed unlikely to be realized immediately. Mutsu urgently telegraphed Oshima, saying that the time for decisive action had arrived and that any excuse could be used to start active operations. The main principle of Japanese policy, as Mutsu said, was that "in military operations, Japan should strike first, but at the same time, it should try to create a situation in which general observers believe that Japan's actions were taken out of necessity."

What was true of Korea in the past is also true of the three northeastern provinces today. Japan's acts of aggression must have a cause and an excuse. However, regardless of whether this cause and excuse can be accepted by the world, Japan must achieve its goal of aggression. Page 77 of the Commission of Enquiry report states, "After Japan filed its reservations in Geneva, it continued to handle the situation in the three northeastern provinces according to its plan." Is this not solid proof? Japan has protested several times about the Chinese people's economic severance with Japan. I only wish to add some comments to the report's interesting statement. Economic severance is just a method of self-defense. Economic severance is only a reaction to external fixed causes and is by no means something that China can restrain. In the past twenty-five years, there have been nine boycott movements against Japanese goods by the Chinese people. Page 115 of the report states, "If this kind of economic severance movement is studied in detail, it is known that each movement is related to a certain confirmed fact event or incident. These events are generally political in nature and are often considered by China to be harmful to its substantial interests or to its national prestige. Therefore, the economic severance of 1931 was directly caused by the Wanbaoshan Incident in June of the same year and the massacre of Koreans in July, and the Shenyang Incident in September of the same year and the Shanghai Incident in January 1932 further intensified it." What should be pointed out here is that the tragic massacre of overseas Chinese in Korea lasted for ten days, from July 3 to July 13, 1931. The massacre sites were all in Korean towns. As a result of the massacre, 147 innocent overseas Chinese died, 546 were injured, 91 were missing, and property losses exceeded Japanese yen 4,000,000.00. At the time of the incident, the Japanese police neither instructed nor stopped it. The Japanese army's attack on Shanghai, the rich center of China in a large East Asian port, killed and injured 24,000 Chinese and destroyed property worth 150 million yuan. And at present, the lives of Chinese people being killed and the property being destroyed in the three northeastern provinces is even more incalculable. Although Shanghai is the center of economic severance activities, after the people of Shanghai heard about the fact that the Japanese army in the three northeastern provinces was fighting without declaring war, they suffered all kinds of pain for five weeks from February to March. Looking at the fact that after the Japanese army withdrew from Shanghai in May, they immediately transferred to the Northeast to continue their killing work, can we still blame them for not taking this retaliatory measure? When I was in Harbin with the Commission of Enquiry in mid-May of this year, I witnessed the 14th Division of the Japanese Army, which was transferred from Shanghai to Harbin, marching past the avenue outside the hotel where I was staying, and the sound of artillery fire and gunfire often entered my ears. I didn't know how many innocent compatriots were killed in a day and a night, but there was no way to stop this tragedy. In this situation, can't we imagine how the people in other central areas of China feel about the tragic fate of their compatriots? The Chinese people's economic severance movement was started and continued to resist the atrocities of the Japanese army. If we consider these facts, we will know that Chinese people, whether individuals or groups, refuse to purchase Japanese goods and participate in boycott activities in order to obtain sufficient effectiveness. They know that their motherland's military equipment is weak and military equipment is insufficient, so they can only adopt this method of self-control to express their anger at Japan's atrocities against China. Those who boycott Japanese goods, especially merchants, inevitably suffer losses themselves when taking this method. This is a kind of self-sacrifice, and there is absolutely no question of seizing Japanese goods owned by the Japanese people. Sometimes, even if there is a misunderstanding, once the facts are clarified, the goods will be returned to the original owner without any difficulty. In this natural mass movement, of course, no government can completely ignore it. In the eyes of the people, the government is the master who protects the safety of the people and prevents them from being invaded by foreign countries. Therefore, on the one hand, the Chinese government deeply feels the atrocities committed by Japan against China, and on the other hand, it has to express sympathy for these economic severance movements and tolerate them. What's more, economic severance is a legitimate strategy of self-defense, and the government cannot ban it. At the same time, the people are extremely angry at Japan's undeclared war against China, so the government sometimes has to order local authorities to guide the people's sentiments and keep them on a legal track, and also pay close attention to protecting the safety of Japanese residents' lives and property. Since the Japanese invasion of the three northeastern provinces, very few incidents of riots against Japanese residents have occurred in China, which is due to this. The Commission of Enquiry report has already confirmed this point. Some people believe that if the Chinese government formally guides the current organized economic severance against Japan, it seems that the issue of responsibility may be raised. Regarding this point, from the Chinese government's perspective, there is absolutely no responsibility to be held accountable. We believe that any form of resistance is reasonable and legal in the face of Japan's brutal and premeditated military aggression. Although we have submitted this case to the international community for peaceful resolution in accordance with the provisions of the covenant, and are quietly waiting for the results, we cannot but try to prevent the Japanese army from continuing its advance as much as possible to aggravate the seriousness of the situation, fearing that any situation, once created, will be regarded as a fait accompli. Since China has adhered to its policy of peace and tolerance unchanged, it has also adopted this peaceful method of resistance, believing that this kind of pressure on the aggressor country does not involve killing or bloodshed, so it is certainly more humane. Otherwise, if force is used against force, the result of killing and bloodshed will be unavoidable. It is expected that economic severance will have a negative impact on Japan, but compared to the tens of thousands of Chinese lives killed and hundreds of millions of Chinese property destroyed by the Japanese army in the three northeastern provinces, Shanghai, and Tianjin, the difference is worlds apart. In this mass movement aroused by patriotic indignation, sometimes there may be two or three radical people who use methods that are not completely in accordance with strict legal regulations in order to make the movement more effective. However, if we think of the fact that the most prosperous three northeastern provinces of China have been occupied by the Japanese army's unreasonable invasion, then the behavior of these people can also be considered reasonable. May I ask what would happen if any other country were to endure the same atrocities to the point of threatening its survival? Therefore, judging from the current situation, even if the Chinese government declares that the current economic severance against Japan throughout China is legal in order to implement the movement in a more orderly manner, it cannot be said to be completely unreasonable. However, the Chinese government has not yet done this, which shows the moderation and tolerance of its policy. We should pay the most attention to the fact that China's economic severance against Japan is out of helplessness. Although economic severance is a method of resisting the atrocities of the Japanese army, it also causes a lot of damage to the Chinese people themselves. China loves peace and always adheres to a peaceful policy in international disputes, so it also hopes to resolve this Japanese invasion through arbitration. Although Japan is stronger than China in terms of military equipment, it is also a member state of the League of Nations. If it can make any demands on China in accordance with one of the peaceful methods stipulated in the League of Nations Covenant, this is what China most hopes for. However, Japanese soldiers did not plan to do this. From the beginning, they adopted force as their policy and implemented their planned invasion plan. Therefore, from the perspective of the Chinese government, the precise implementation of economic severance against Japan is necessary. Moreover, since the League of Nations' remedial measures take time, this method of resistance cannot be delayed. The experience of the past fourteen months seems to have confirmed the accuracy of this view. The Japanese government has not only failed to fulfill its obligations accepted in the Executive Yuan resolutions of September 30 and December 2 of last year, to withdraw the Japanese army into the South Manchuria Railway Zone, but has intensified its activities. To this day, there is not a single place in the three northeastern provinces that is not under the iron heel of the Japanese army. And the League of Nations, during this long period, has not yet found an effective way to prevent the Japanese army from increasing the severity of the local situation politically or militarily, or to force the Japanese army to fulfill its promise to withdraw into the railway zone in accordance with the resolution's claims. If we do not recognize China's use of economic severance to resist the atrocities of the Japanese army, it is tantamount to not recognizing peaceful and legal self-defense methods. What's more, in the modern world economy, the use of protective tariffs, distribution systems, and restrictions on exchange rates has all been recognized as legal. These methods are still regarded as legal self-defense strategies against economic aggression. Since the nature of China's economic severance is very similar, why can't it be allowed to be used as a self-defense strategy to resist military aggression? As for whether China's economic severance against Japan conflicts with friendship with Japan and treaty obligations, this issue is not worth asking today. To resolve this issue, we must first ask whether Sino-Japanese relations can still be considered friendly under the various atrocities committed by the Japanese government in Korea, where it massacred countless overseas Chinese, and in Manchuria, Shanghai, and other places, where it occupied Chinese territory, killed countless Chinese lives, and destroyed countless Chinese property. Under the circumstances that Japan intends to violate all treaty obligations, should China still strive to fulfill its unilateral obligations? If we obtain an answer to the latter question, then the former question can be omitted. I sincerely hope that the above points will shed some light on the consideration of the issue of China's economic severance against Japan and on the true meaning of this movement. Although China's national ideology has developed extremely rapidly in recent years, it actually has no xenophobic implications. (To be continued)

The Establishment of Lishan County is Added in Eastern Hubei 72

The Headquarters Stipulates Methods, Jiang Zhangji is Appointed as the County Magistrate

A dispatch from Hankou states that the Commander-in-Chief Headquarters for Suppressing Bandits in the Three Provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui has recently decided to add Lishan County in the area between Huangma and Jingfu Counties in Eastern Hubei in order to facilitate administration. Jiang Zhangji has been appointed as the first county magistrate of the county. Because it is the beginning of the establishment and affairs are complicated, special methods were formulated on the 15th, ordering the Hubei Provincial Government to comply. The methods are as follows: 1) In terms of geographical relations, the county should be under the jurisdiction of the Administrative Inspector of the Fourth District of Hubei. 2) Before the county seal is transferred by the Ministry of the Interior for issuance, a wooden seal will be temporarily issued by the headquarters to show faith. The county magistrate will come to the headquarters to receive it and report the date of its use for future reference. 3) In addition to the establishment fee and the initial investigation fee of 3,000 yuan, the first month's expenses and subsidies totaling 2,250 yuan, totaling 5,250 yuan, should be drawn by the county magistrate from the headquarters' finance department. In the future, monthly expenses and subsidies totaling 2,250 yuan should be budgeted by the county magistrate and directly submitted to the provincial government for issuance. 4) The headquarters should send a committee member to delineate the county boundary, and the county magistrate should also serve as the committee member. However, the boundary between the county and Jingfu County is slightly different. The county boundary should be used as the standard, and the county magistrate of Jingfu County and the surveying committee members should carefully delineate and report for investigation. 5) After the county magistrate takes office, all organizational steps and construction matters should be explained in detail in a list and submitted to the headquarters and the relevant provincial and district officials for verification. 6) All other matters shall be handled in accordance with the new establishment guidelines for newly established counties in the recovered area promulgated by the headquarters. (December 15th)

Page 7

The United States After the Election 73

The United States of North America, hailed as the world's financial king, dominating the world with its gold standard policy, possesses a quarter of the world's cash, yet this is insufficient to remedy its practical difficulties and overcome the current panic. President Hoover, in his campaign speeches, claimed that the panic had reached its lowest point and would gradually improve. He also asserted that the economic decline in the United States was not the fault of the U.S. itself, but rather the influence of the world economy.

Undoubtedly, most Americans believed his claims. However, anyone who has been to the United States and observed the general situation knows that ordinary Americans have a very faint interest in politics. They have no particularly strong support for or opposition to either Hoover or Roosevelt. However, they are indeed tired of the Republican Party's rule and want a change. Moreover, Hoover's tricks to stimulate market prosperity have not been successful, failing to maintain public support. Therefore, the Republican presidential candidate could not but lose the election.

Roosevelt will be the master of the White House after March next year, and various government offices will have a new set of people. The Democratic Party, based on farmers and energized by the Ku Klux Klan, is resuming power. What will become of this, it is still difficult to say. Although the current president cannot fully insist on the policies he advocates, he is very careful about the aftermath, especially preserving the interests of bankers, leaving a good impression and paving the way for the Republican Party's future. Although President Hoover is promoting everywhere, saying that the "economic panic" has gradually passed and a good market is coming soon, he is still vigilant. For example, the wealthy state of New York is requesting assistance for the poor every day. Not only is the effect minimal, but even the state government's salaries cannot be paid. The federal government plans to levy a sales tax on all goods (except food), but it is feared that merely increasing taxes will not be enough to balance the budget. Therefore, a further reduction in federal officials' salaries is necessary, reportedly cutting salaries by 11%. The image of a land of gold, which we imagined before visiting America, contrasts sharply with the hardship faced by its ordinary people today. Though better than that of our homeland across the ocean, and despite higher material enjoyment, the sudden shift from salary reduction to unemployment is a scene of great panic.

The end of June this year marks the end of the fiscal year. A comprehensive calculation of the loans borrowed due to the panic over the past year totals a staggering 3.3 billion U.S. dollars, including 615.6 million U.S. dollars in Treasury notes and 272.5 million U.S. dollars in Treasury bills. Securities maturing in September this year amount to 712 million U.S. dollars. Because there are various conditions in the market that provide for use (such as excessive idle funds and no place to invest), the government's issuance of public bonds is very convenient. Therefore, in addition to issuing 400 million U.S. dollars in securities with an interest rate of 1.25%, it also issued 750 million U.S. dollars in five-year notes with an interest rate of 3.25%. The number of applications within a short period of time exceeded seven times. The amount of short-term loans that have matured recently is as follows:

Maturity Date Type Amount Interest Rate

(Thousands of USD)

October 15, 1932 Securities 33,300 3.25% (Thousands of USD)

December 5, 1932 Notes 600,300 3.25% (Thousands of USD)

March 15, 1933 Securities 660,700 3.75%

It is easy to convert these short-term loans into long-term or medium-term loans, as long as the interest rate is not below 3%. Although public debt increases year by year and raising public debt is easy, the decrease in tax revenue indicates industrial decline. Even if public debt can be increased, it is not a good sign.

The Democratic Party's policy toward the Orient, especially for us Chinese living in foreign countries, deserves particular attention. Within the Democratic Party, there are indeed some who advocate peace, concessions to Japan, revising immigration laws, and abolishing differential treatment towards Japan. They advocate returning the Atlantic Fleet to its original formation, but still insist on "Open Door" policy and will not give up the Eastern market. On the issue of Philippine independence, there are also two different views within the Democratic Party. One faction believes that the Cutting proposal, which allows the Philippines to be independent after eight years, is too long. They believe that the island should be allowed independence within the next 40 months. First, it conforms to the Democratic Party's consistent advocacy, and second, it takes the opportunity to gain Britain's favor and break up the alliance between Britain and Japan. On the surface, the desire to keep overseas territories under the American flag and not allow them free independence runs counter to the principles and ideals that the United States has always held. Therefore, allowing the Philippines to be independent is inevitable. On the other hand, some believe that the U.S. Congress does not have the power to allow the Philippine Islands to be independent, because the Federal Constitution does not grant such power to Congress. Therefore, the power to allow the Philippines to be independent lies with all the people of the United States. Unless the Constitution is amended first, Congress has no right to pass this case. Furthermore, the faction advocating Philippine independence does not advocate giving up the special right to station troops in the Philippines. Although most Americans are tired of war, they are unwilling to relax their hold on commercial and investment interests.

Take the issue of European war debts as an example. In terms of financial losses and the credit of the financial capitalists in their own party, they cannot but strongly demand repayment. However, in terms of commercial interests and the sales of industrial products to Europe, if funds are forcibly repatriated, the European market will become more depressed, and the U.S. economic panic will be even more difficult to recover. Even U.S. bankers, who are hailed as experts in capital management, cannot help but seek short-term gains and will probably insist on collecting debts. Whether they can collect the more than 270 million U.S. dollars in European war debts that are due on December 15 is of course a problem. They do not care about the future and just want to do their best to collect debts now. From the perspective of Washington, they generally believe that they can be collected. (November 18, 1932, Washington)

Southwestern Preparations for the Qinyu Railway 74

The entire line from Qinzhou, Guangdong, through Guangxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan to Chongqing is 1,850 miles long, divided into five sections for construction, estimated to be completed in six years. Guangzhou Communication: The Southwest Political Affairs Committee recently resolved to develop southwestern transportation and prepare for the construction of the Qinyu Railway in the five provinces of Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan. It also telegraphed each provincial government to send one representative to Guangzhou to organize a road construction committee. Guangxi Province recently appointed Wang Xunzhi as a preparatory committee member, and Guangdong Province recently appointed Chen Guoquan as a preparatory committee member. As for Guizhou Province, a representative was sent to Guangzhou by Wang Jialie to negotiate. However, due to the sudden change in the political situation in Guizhou and the ongoing stalemate in the Sichuan war, Sichuan and Guizhou have not yet sent out preparatory members. As for the road construction plan, Li Xiangen, Li Xisheng, Zhang Renmin, Mai Huanzhang, and others have recently been appointed to be responsible for review. The plan is as follows:

Total Mileage of the Entire Route 75

The Qinyu Railway starts from Qinzhou in Guangdong Province and ends at the border of Guangxi Province. Within Guangdong, the route occupies 35 miles. Within Guangxi, it occupies 321 miles. Within Guizhou, there are two lines, A and B. (1) Line A occupies 214 miles. (2) Line B occupies 340 miles. Within Sichuan, to Chongqing, there are also two lines, A and B. (1) Line A occupies 267 miles. (2) Line B occupies 446 miles.

Construction Expenses 76

1. Opening and surveying costs, including preparation fees, instrument purchase fees, surveyor salaries, etc., require approximately 2,500 silver dollars per mile.

2. Land purchase costs require approximately 1,600 silver dollars per mile.

3. Construction engineering costs, including roadbed, bridge culvert, ditch, tunnel, etc., require approximately 32,000 silver dollars per mile.

4. Rail and sleeper costs, including rail and accessory costs, sleeper costs, transportation costs, and installation costs, require approximately 48,000 silver dollars per mile.

5. Building construction costs, including locomotive factory and machine costs, require 1,500 silver dollars per mile.

6. Vehicle purchase costs, including locomotive, passenger car, freight car, guard car, etc., require 6,000 silver dollars per mile.

7. Telegraph and telephone installation costs require 600 silver dollars per mile. In total, each mile requires approximately 92,200 silver dollars in labor and material costs.

Construction in Sections 77

In order to share the burden equally and avoid provincial boundaries, it is proposed that each province construct one-fifth of the road. Taking Line A as an example, the total length of the Qinyu route is approximately 2,000 miles, divided into five sections for construction. The route of each section is recorded as follows: The first section, Guangdong, starts from Qinxian County, Guangdong, and passes through Yongning, Longguan, Silin, to Fengyi. The second section, Guangxi, starts from Fengyi, Guangxi, and ends in Xingyi. The third section, Yunnan, starts from Xingyi and passes through Luoping, Qujing, Xuanwei, Yunnan, to Kedu River. The fourth section, Guizhou, starts from Kedu River and passes through Weining, Hezhang, Bijie, Guizhou, to Xuyong, Sichuan. The fifth section starts from Xuyong and passes through Gusong, Naxi, Longchang, Yongchuan, to Chongqing.

Survey Route 78

Appoint one chief engineer, two senior engineers, two deputy engineers, and several technicians, technical assistants, and surveyors to organize two survey teams. First, the chief engineer will re-examine the route to be built in the province for one week. Then, the two senior engineers will divide into teams to conduct a detailed survey of the line, to be completed within one year. According to the plan, the first year will be to complete the survey route, the second year to complete the construction of the roadbed, the third and fourth years to complete the construction of bridges and lay sleepers and rails, the fifth year to complete the station factory, and the sixth year to open to traffic. (December 9)

A Scare in Yantai

Liu's Independent Brigade's Cannonballs Mishandled, Prisoners Take the Opportunity to Escape 79

Jinan Communication: Liu Zhennian's troops have been disembarking in Yantai for days, heading to Fujian and Zhejiang, leaving only the independent brigade to depart last. On the morning of April 15, over 700 boxes of mortar shells stored by the 8th Regiment of the brigade in Xihai Dam exploded due to the carelessness of the guarding soldiers, who knocked over a kerosene lamp, igniting the bedding and setting off the shells. The explosion shook the city. Unaware of the truth, citizens panicked, and order was disrupted. Fortunately, the Public Security Team and Security Team announced along the streets, and people's hearts were settled. During the incident, the Fushan District Court, located very close to the fire, had over 70 prisoners in the detention center take the opportunity to escape, seizing the guns from the gate guards. The navy and public security bureau are currently conducting a strict search for the fugitives. Zhang Kuiwen, the Yantai Public Security Bureau Chief, sent a telegram to the provincial government yesterday reporting everything. The original telegram is reproduced below: To Chairman Han Jun of the Provincial Government, De Mi: Today, the 8th Regiment of the Independent Brigade received and stored over 700 boxes of mortar shells in Xihai Dam. At 5:50, the guarding soldiers in the regiment's letter room knocked over a kerosene lamp, igniting the bedding and detonating the shells. People were terrified, not knowing what happened. Upon learning of this, I immediately led the Security Team to rescue. However, during the explosion, order was greatly disrupted. The Fushan District Court, located very close to the fire, had over 70 prisoners in the detention center take the opportunity to escape, seizing one gun from the gate guards. I am currently supervising each branch bureau team to cooperate with the navy in a strict search. Further details will be reported in due course. Respectfully submitted, Your subordinate Zhang Kuiwen kowtows respectfully. (April 16)

Guangdong Province Develops Huangpu Port City

The First Phase of Land Acquisition Has Been Surveyed, and an Administrative City Area Will Be Developed Outside the Port 80

Guangzhou Communication: Guangdong Province has been developing Huangpu Commercial Port for several years. Later, the port development matters were transferred to the Guangdong Provincial River Management Committee. In the past two years, it has completed the surveying of 11,145 acres of land required for the first phase. A 20-year plan and map for the port city have now been drafted and sent to various agencies for review. In the future, the government plans to recover private land at fair prices, first setting up a private land registration office for valuation and processing. It also plans to first build a Huangpu-Yuzhu Market, a Huangpu Highway, and six 3,000-foot cargo warehouses at the pier. Secondly, it will develop streets by zoning. According to the current water depth at the entrance, which is about 22 feet deep, ships under 5,000 tons can navigate unimpeded. The main points of the port city development are as follows: (1) Huangpu Port City refers to both Huangpu Port and Huangpu City. Huangpu Port is the commercial area of Huangpu Port, and Huangpu City is the urban area of Huangpu Port. They are unified in governance. An administrative agency will be established in the urban area, directly under the Guangdong Provincial Government. The port is designated as a tax port, so that customs duties can be used for administrative expenses and to protect the province's nascent industries. (2) Huangpu has a deep-water bay that can accommodate ocean-going ships and is decided to be developed as a first-class commercial port. (3) The commercial port is located in the Yuzhu Market area, so as to connect with the Guangzhou shipping line. (4) The Huangpu Port area has a land area of 182,290 acres and a water area of 36,486 acres, totaling 218,750 acres. Huangpu Port itself includes Yuzhu, Changzhou, Shalu, and three other locations, including Tonggusha, Shark Island, Dajisha, Dragon Boat Sand, Hongshengsha, Doggy Sand, and Beidisha, with a total land area of 64,860 acres and a water area of 14,960 acres, totaling 79,820 acres. (5) Huangpu Port City is divided into the following areas: port industry area, port municipal area, heavy industry area, light industry area, two types of commercial areas (large and small), three types of residential areas (A, B, and C), agricultural and forestry area, parks and playgrounds, and public cemeteries. (6) The locations of each area are planned as follows: The administrative area is selected south of the Shanan Village, which is the central point. The industrial area is planned to be located west of Wakugang, north of the Yuzhu Market and Lian Shi Creek Village, and between Shigan Huanxi Village, to facilitate land and water transportation. The drop-off area is planned to be south of Leifeng Mountain, Xixi, Wenchong, Wenyuan, and Shuanggua, located south of the future Guangshan Railway. Type A residential areas are scattered around Feilongling, Baiqiling, Zhuangyuan Mountain, Shetanggang, Niushan, Shuanggua, Houdishan, and Luogang. Type B residential areas are on the five islands of Shark Island, Dajisha, Dragon Boat Sand, Hongshengsha, and Changzhou. Type C residential areas are located north of the Guangshan Railway line, south of the Guangjiu Railway, east of Cangshi, and west of Daoyong, in the Hengsha area, and near Longbucun Huanxi Village. The above areas are urban areas. The port area is located south of Huangpu Highway, east of Yuji Fort, and west of Daoyongkou, with five parts of the Huangpu deep-water bay boat harbor and inland river boat harbor.

The outer port berth embankment line is 1,100 meters long, the inner port berth embankment line is 3,000 meters long, the Huangpu deep-water bay boat harbor embankment line is 2,768 meters long, and the inland river boat harbor berth embankment line is 7,775 meters long. (December 12)

Fujian Province Plans to Establish Two Ordinary Municipalities

Fuzhou and Xiamen 81

Fuzhou Communication: The Fujian Provincial Government recently stated that Fuzhou and Xiamen are both important commercial ports on the southeast coast. Fuzhou has a population of 330,000 and local tax revenue of approximately 1 million yuan per year. Xiamen has a total population of 210,000 (including the two districts of Heshan and Gulangyu) and local tax revenue of over 300,000 yuan per year. It is necessary to establish ordinary municipalities in accordance with the provisions of the Municipal Organization Law. It is now planned to take the areas under the jurisdiction of the Fuzhou Public Security Bureau in Nanbaicheng as the center, and then according to the mountain and river terrain, the Fuzhou urban area will start from Kuaiqi at the foot of Gushan in the east, along Dongling and Tangling, directly to Beiling, and then west around Bailong Baofu to Dafushan, across the Minjiang River, from Huaianjiao to the Southwest Port, along the Daolong River, to Xiadou, with an area of over 300 square miles. The current Minhou County will be divided into Min County and Houguan County. The Min County seat will be moved to the Majiang area (south of Fuzhou City) in the lower reaches of the Minjiang River, and the Houguan County seat will be moved to the Baisha area (west of Fuzhou City) in the upper reaches of the Minjiang River. The Xiamen City area will also be combined with the areas under the jurisdiction of the Xiamen Public Security Bureau and the two areas of Heshan Gulangyu under the jurisdiction of the Siming County Government. Siming County will be abolished. A statement has been drafted and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. It is rumored that He Gonggan and Chen Peikun are the most popular candidates for mayor in the future. In addition, the provincial government plans to establish municipal bureaus in important counties upstream and downstream, such as Zhangzhou, Quanzhou, Xinghua, Yanping, Shaowu, Jian'ou, and Sandu, to handle local transportation, sanitation, public welfare, and other matters, so as to advance simultaneously with the 19th Route Army's plan to revive the rural areas of western Fujian, in order to achieve prosperity in both urban and rural areas.

Songjiang Finance Bureau Official Temporarily Exempt from Surveillance 82

The Finance Bureau embezzled over 60,000 yuan of special funds for provincial education. After the department head Yang Zixin verified this, he reported to the Niuchu Office. A telegram ordered County Chief Shen to strictly supervise Feng Gengbai, the outgoing director of the planning section of the Finance Bureau, and order him to clear the account. He was not allowed to leave before clearing the account, etc. Upon receiving the order from the Finance Department, Director Feng was ordered to handle the handover with the bureau chief. County Chief Shen secretly instructed Chen Rongchu, the police captain, to send police to supervise. It is now known that Director Feng, due to the numerous handover funds and all closing events, was being supervised by the police, which restricted his freedom. He specially invited the owner of Zhongdetang Pharmacy to act as guarantor and clarified to the county government that he should be exempt from supervision so that he could work in peace. It is rumored that County Chief Shen has approved the request and ordered the police chief to handle it.

Minutes of the Qingzhang Custody Meeting 83

The county government held the third regular meeting of the Qingzhang Custody Committee yesterday. Shen Yong, Shen Bingchao, Cai Zhongyu, Gu Guangyi, and others attended. Suzhou Yutai Steamer Kidnapping Victim Escapes Danger 84

The details of the lake bandits robbing arms and injuring police and kidnapping the Yutai liner in Huangyang Bay, Dongshan, and kidnapping Xi Chunqiao, manager of Shanghai Dalun Silk and Satin Store, and Zhou Yinggao of Tiancheng Silk and Satin Bureau have been detailed in previous reports. It is now known that the two hostages, Xi and Zhou, were sent to Maoqi Port (near Hengjing Township, about 40 to 50 li from Suzhou) by bandits in a small fishing boat on the evening of the 17th and released ashore. They have now returned to their homes in Dongshan. In addition, a fisherman, Song Xiuqing, and his son, Pu Cai, were kidnapped with their boat by bandits on September 26. Pu Cai was released on the 4th of this month, while Xiuqing was forced to row the boat. First, they went to Ducun to kidnap two men and one woman. Because the three hostages were poor and had no money, they were released immediately. Later, they robbed the Yutai steamer. Now Song has also been released. According to him, there were six bandit ships when the liner was robbed. Except for the boat he was rowing, the other five ships were gathered in Huangyang Bay.

Gangs of Bandits Harass the Taihu Lake Area 85

The day before yesterday (17th), a large gang of over a hundred lake bandits was discovered near Hengjing, along Taihu Lake, intending to rob villages along the lake. Captain Pei of the 7th Water Police Team immediately led his team in pursuit overnight, but found nothing. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 18th, 30 to 40 bandits arrived at Jiangzhuang in South Taihu Lake, robbing two families, Zhou Chunshan and Shi Dunxiang, and kidnapping a woman, Zhou Shen, and fleeing towards Taihu Lake. The water and land police teams will set off together today to launch a large-scale campaign to exterminate them in one fell swoop.

Silk Industry Representatives Petition for Tax Reduction 86

The silk, satin, and silk weaving industries in Wu County, in view of the fact that rayon is a necessary raw material for domestic goods, and that the current import tax rate on rayon is 100%, the National Government is about to revise the import tax rate. Therefore, they sent representatives Shi Yunqing, Hua Fuqing, Zhang Shupeng, and others to Beijing to petition the Ministries of Industry and Finance, requesting a reduction in the import tax rate on rayon. Director Zhang of the Ministry of Industry agreed to submit the request when revising the tariff. The representatives were satisfied and returned to Suzhou yesterday.

Wuxi 88

Mixing Mercury in Noodles to Kill His Wife

You Liangzong, the owner of Dachangyuan North-South Grocery Store under the Beimenwai Bridge, was naturally tyrannical and often abused his wife, Huang Suzhen, in every way. Suzhen, unable to endure it any longer, filed a lawsuit with the County Court, requesting that You be detained and severely punished. Unexpectedly, You had ulterior motives and repeatedly considered murdering his wife, but ultimately had no good plan. Recently, he entrusted someone to mediate with Huang Suzhen, revoking the court case, stating that You would subsidize her with 15 yuan for food and lodging each month. Huang Suzhen agreed, and they lived in Wanchang Small Foreign Goods Store in Sibao Alley, and the couple was as good as ever. At about 8:00 yesterday morning, You Liangzong saw a bowl of overnight noodles in the kitchen and suddenly hatched a poisonous plan, secretly placing a large amount of mercury in the noodles, and persuading Suzhen to eat them. When she had finished eating, she felt unbearable abdominal pain and shouted loudly. You's actions were exposed, and he ran upstairs, escaping from the upstairs window. Suzhen had no choice but to report to the 5th Branch of the Public Security Bureau for investigation and treatment at the Maternity Department of the Guangfu Menwai Hou Taipingxiang Hospital. After the hospital doctors performed surgery, she was able to turn the corner.

Nine Houses Burned in a Fire on Yuan Tong Road 89

Since the beginning of winter, the city has had very little snow, the weather has been dry, and there have been frequent fires. At 3:30 yesterday afternoon, a barber shop named Xin Rongxuan, opened by Hu Fengbao near the police kiosk on Yuan Tong Road in Guanghoumen, suddenly caught fire. The fire spread to the neighboring blacksmith shop, Yuan Yongxing Bicycle Shop, Meihua Western Clothing Store, and Yang Zhengda Rattan Shop. The wind was strong at the time, and the fire grew with the help of the wind, leaping over Xinmin Road and affecting nine houses, including Hengji Rickshaw Shop, Luo Wanxu Round Bucket Workshop, the Yu family's sesame cake shop, and Sun Yuxing Rattan Store. Fire brigades from various sections responded to the alarm, driving dragons to the scene one after another and working hard to extinguish the fire. The total loss amounted to tens of thousands of yuan, with Meihua Western Clothing Store suffering the heaviest losses. Also today (18th) at 4:00 am, Wang, the wife of Chen Daju in Shiputou outside the West Gate, started a fire due to the careless use of fire while making tea, causing a fire that spread to six or seven thatched huts belonging to Xu Shanchang and others. The fire brigades from Districts 1, 2, 3, and 4 in the West District arrived at the scene to extinguish the fire. Also, Zhou Maorong and six other families in Shijiatang, District 15, were careless last night, suffering losses of several thousand yuan.

Changzhou 90

A Large Batch of Poison Pills Seized from Empty Coffin

Fang Qi, the police captain of Wuyi County Government, received a secret report on the 17th that a large batch of poison pills were hidden in a certain ancestral hall. He immediately joined the police officers of the 1st Branch of the Public Security Bureau to search the Liu family's ancestral hall in Dongxiatang. Opium is exclusively sold by Xin Xin Company in Nantong, but only stamped goods are allowed, and smuggled goods must still be investigated.

Xiaoshan 93

Peasants Petition for Exemption of Land Tax

Peasants in eastern Xiaoshan, due to the county's decision to levy a tax for river management, have repeatedly petitioned the county government to retract the order, but have been denied. Now, the peasants of the area, affected by the current situation and disasters in recent years, are already on the verge of collapse. Although this year is slightly more bountiful, they are still struggling due to low grain prices. They held a meeting yesterday to discuss the matter and appointed Sun Zhengkang and ten others as a petitioning group to go to the provincial capital to petition, and will not stop until the goal of cancellation is achieved.

The Xixing Public Security Bureau Police Station in Xiaoshan was surrounded and destroyed by workers from the Highway Bureau on the 14th. At that time, the police station telegraphed the county government, which immediately dispatched a patrol team to make arrests. Ningbo 95

Naval Police Transport Smoked Opium and Resist Arrest

When the Xin Jiang Tian steamboat arrived at the port yesterday morning on the 16th, five naval escort police officers, including Zheng Dezheng, were carrying smoked opium on behalf of others to a certain location. However, the matter was not kept secret and was discovered. It was immediately reported to the Fifth Branch of the Jiangbei Public Security Bureau. After receiving the report, the bureau immediately sent Inspector Zheng to supervise Police Chief Li to secretly go to the railway station and checkpoints at Malan Bridge to conduct strict investigations and ordered the police on duty to pay attention. At around 9 o'clock, Naval Police Hu Jinting was found carrying a large package of smoked opium, and was being protected by other naval police, including Zheng Zhengde, while passing through Manao Road. This was spotted by police officer Guo Jiasheng, who was stationed there by the Fifth Branch. He immediately went forward to investigate, but the naval police not only refused to be inspected, but also attacked with iron rulers. Officer Guo knew that he was no match and, while resisting, frantically blew his police whistle. Inspector Zheng and the police chief heard the alarm and rushed to arrest them. Naval Police Zheng Dezheng then used a pistol to resist arrest. After a fierce resistance, Naval Police Zheng Dezheng, Li Yulin, Hu Xinting, Yang Guodong, and Li Jiaguo were finally captured. A package of smoked opium weighing 45 taels was also found on Hu Xinting, and two eight-inch Browning pistols, sixteen bullets, two magazines, an iron ruler, and four naval police team insignia were seized and sent to the bureau for investigation.

Page 8

Various Organizations in This City Stop Celebrating the New Year

The Municipal Government Has Already Issued Orders to Its Subordinates to Comply 96

The Shanghai Municipal Government received an order from the National Government yesterday, stating that during this time of national crisis, all citizens and the government should endure hardship and strive for revival. The New Year of the 22nd year should not be celebrated. The Municipal Government immediately issued orders to all bureaus and agencies to comply. It is said that at that time, in addition to the Municipal Government hosting foreign guests and the Mayor paying respects to foreign officials stationed in Shanghai, all other agencies will stop celebrating the New Year.

Fuhai Steamer Gunfire Incident 102

The Fisheries Bureau Misunderstood Fuhai, Fuhai Misunderstood the Navy, and the Fisheries Bureau Also Misunderstood the Navy. This Case Is Under Negotiation.

The Fuhai patrol ship of the Marine Fisheries Administration of the Jiangzhe District of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce had a misunderstanding with the Navy the day before yesterday and opened fire. Yesterday, the Navy soldiers had already withdrawn, and the shipyard had sent a letter to the bureau for negotiation. We will now record the details as follows:

The Navy Withdraws 103

Since the Fuhai patrol ship opened fire on the Navy the day before yesterday, the Jiangnan and Jiangkang small steamboats of the Navy have approached the Datong Pier. In order to determine the responsibility for right and wrong and to avoid the expansion of the situation and causing unexpected disputes, the Navy authorities ordered all the guards on the two small steamboats to withdraw on the night of the day before yesterday. Weisheng also stopped its operations, so the situation yesterday was more relaxed.

Cause of the Conflict 104

The cause of the conflict the day before yesterday was entirely a misunderstanding and was very complicated. The Fisheries Bureau has a total of four patrol ships: Qing'an, Haiying, Biaohai, and Fuhai, which are all protecting fisheries in the outer seas. The Fuhai ship was also in Dinghai a month ago, protecting fishing boats. The bureau recently responded to the request of the Yongfeng Frozen Seafood Company in this city and agreed to dispatch the Fuhai ship to protect the company's frozen seafood on the sea surface, so it immediately ordered the ship to sail to Shanghai. However, at that time, the ship was protecting fisheries between Shengshan and Dinghai and could not return immediately. Later, Zhou Bingkui, the acting director of the bureau, personally went to Dinghai to meet the ship's captain, Guo Wei, and ordered him to sail to Shanghai immediately. After discussing the supply of food and pay for the ship, Zhou left for Shanghai first.

Delay in Arriving in Shanghai 105

After Zhou left Dinghai, the Fuhai ship continued to engage in fishing protection work there (the ship's merchants have a treaty stipulating that it cannot protect other fishing vessels before the protection period expires). When Fuhai planned to return, a "Da Dui" fishing merchant reported that fishing boats off Shenjiaxing had been robbed and requested the ship to suppress the bandits. The captain of the ship felt that it was difficult not to deal with it, so he sailed the ship to Shenjiamen to suppress the bandits and informed the Shanghai bureau. In the middle, due to the time spent suppressing the bandits, there was some delay, and it was not until the 14th of this month that it arrived in Shanghai and dropped anchor in the Jiangqiao Pudong area of the South City.

The Fisheries Bureau is Furious 106

The Fisheries Bureau was furious because the ship had repeatedly been ordered to sail to Shanghai but was still slow to act, delaying the time, which caused the bureau's previous promise to the Yongfeng Frozen Seafood Company to send a ship for protection to be delayed. The company had already requested another ship for protection, so it was very angry about the ship's delayed actions and disregard for the bureau's orders.

The Misunderstanding Arises 107

At the same time, it was rumored that the bureau would ask the Navy to pursue the ship and disarm it because it had disregarded the bureau's orders. Therefore, the ship could not help but feel uneasy after arriving in Shanghai. It happened that the Navy sent personnel with guards to the ship the day before yesterday to negotiate outstanding payments, which made the ship even more convinced that they were coming to disarm it, so it was very frightened. Thus, a misunderstanding arose, and gunfire was opened, almost leading to a major incident.

Report to the Bureau 108

When the conflict between the ship and the Navy occurred the day before yesterday, Wang Zhiliang, the director of the Fisheries Bureau's Dinghai office (currently in Shanghai), learned of it. Because he did not understand the truth, he went to the bureau to meet with Acting Director Zhou and reported that two gray ships full of soldiers had come to the Fuhai ship to disarm it. He asked if it was dispatched by the director. Zhou was very surprised at the time because he had not issued such an order. He asked if there was an official document, and if there was no official document, they should resist.

Serious Negotiations 109

When Director Wang reported to Acting Director Zhou, it was after the Fuhai ship had fired a shot. The Navy felt that the ship's actions were strange and unusual, and it was inconvenient to board the ship again to avoid further incidents. At that time, it immediately retreated to another location and withdrew on order that night, and the serious situation stopped immediately. Yesterday, the Navy authorities stated that the ship belonged to the Fisheries Bureau and that the outstanding payments had been repeatedly demanded from the bureau without any response. It was unreasonable to send personnel to the ship to negotiate and open fire without asking the reason. Therefore, although yesterday was Sunday, Deputy Director Chen Zaofan still went to the office to work and ordered the secretary of the shipyard to send a letter to the bureau for serious negotiations. If there was still no effect, effective measures would be taken. The letter was issued yesterday in the name of the Jiangnan Shipyard of the Navy Department.

Fisheries Bureau's Statement 110

According to the Fisheries Bureau's statement to the China News Agency, the outstanding payments had long been submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for transfer to the Ministry of Finance, but they had not been received to date. The bureau's funding was extremely difficult, so the shipyard's current funds could not be raised. Even the salaries of the bureau's current employees were borrowed from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce by several thousand yuan to be paid, so the bureau was unable to repay the debt. In the bureau's current situation, it was truly helpless. In addition to the Jiangnan Shipyard, the Haiying patrol ship of the bureau had also been unable to pay the repair fees to the Qiu Xin Factory years ago.

Shanghai-Tianjin Route Will Open 111

Scheduled to Return Three Times a Week Starting on New Year's Day Next Year

The Shanghai-Tianjin aviation route, which has been planned for a long time, has been delayed until now due to the Qingdao airport issue. Now that all the procedures have been completed, it has been decided to officially fly starting on New Year's Day next year. The details are as follows:

Qingdao Airport Resolves The Shanghai-Tianjin air route is sponsored by the China National Aviation Corporation. Since its preparation, it has been eight months. The various airports along the route, such as Haizhou and Tianjin, have long been built. However, the land for the Qingdao station was leased by the Japanese, so the Ministry of Communications sent personnel to Qingdao several times to negotiate the recovery, but without success. It was not until Qingdao Mayor Shen Honglie negotiated the recovery of about 400 mu of land, paying the Japanese 20,000 yuan.

Official Launch After Zhu Jia驊 took over as chairman of the company, he transferred Dai Enji to succeed him as general manager. After taking office, Dai actively developed the business by reorganizing the internal affairs. He paid special attention to the Shanghai-Tianjin line, and planned to open it as soon as possible to facilitate transportation. Therefore, since the Qingdao airport was resolved, he supervised his subordinates to go to Qingdao to handle the installation of radios, etc., and restored the airports along the line. The original aviation station built at Tianjin Airport had already been destroyed, and it was originally planned to be rebuilt. However, in order to save expenses, it was decided to rent houses nearby for passengers to rest and for staff to work, which was more convenient in terms of procedures and allowed for earlier preparation. The route is expected to be officially launched on New Year's Day next year for passenger and mail transportation.

Full Route Distance The total distance of the route is slightly less than 700 miles, with four stations: Shanghai, Haizhou, Qingdao, and Tianjin. From Shanghai to Haizhou is 270 miles, Haizhou to Qingdao is 150 miles, and Qingdao to Tianjin is 270 miles. In the future, the number of flights along the line will be temporarily three round trips per week, and then increased depending on the flight performance.

Ticket Prices After the full route is opened, the departure times and prices are still under consideration. However, according to the investigation by the China News Agency, the approximate prices are 80 yuan from Shanghai to Haizhou, 120 yuan to Qingdao, and 220 yuan to Dalian. Haizhou to Qingdao is 40 yuan, Qingdao to Tianjin is 100 yuan, and Haizhou to Tianjin is 120 yuan.

Flight Times (Northbound Flight) Shanghai departs at 7:45 am, arrives at Haizhou at 10:45 am, Haizhou departs at 10:55 am, arrives at Qingdao at 12:15 pm, Qingdao departs at 12:30 pm, and arrives at Tianjin at 3:30 pm. (Southbound Flight) Tianjin departs at 8:00 am, arrives at Qingdao at 11:00 am, Qingdao departs at 11:15 am, arrives at Haizhou at 12:35 pm, Haizhou departs at 12:45 pm, and arrives at Shanghai at 3:45 pm. (The above times and fares are said to be subject to change.)

It is heard that the Russians are currently planning to open a regular shipping line between Shanghai and Vladivostok to facilitate the transportation of goods.

The Story of the Two Railway Lines' Employees Requesting Wartime Bonuses 115

The case of employees from the Japanese-controlled Jinghu (Nanjing-Shanghai), Huhangyong (Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo) railway lines requesting the issuance of loss relief loans to employees serving in war zones failed to gain approval from the Ministry of Railways, leading to gatherings and detentions of trains, which has already been reported in the newspapers. Reporters stationed in Nanjing, considering that the nation is currently facing severe difficulties, and the sudden occurrence of such incidents is extremely unfortunate, and the details of this incident will certainly be of concern to people in society, inquired with the Ministry of Railways for detailed records of the matter's initiation and handling. After investigating, this case originated after the January 28th Incident this year. All employees of the Jinghu and Huhangyong railway lines, angered by the violent Japanese occupation of Shanghai, risked their lives to perform their duties. The Minister of Railways, concerned about the employees in the war zone, sent personnel to express condolences and instructed the railway bureaus to specially commend and console those employees of the two lines who had served bravely and loyally, provide generous compensation to the injured and deceased, and award 30,000 yuan to those who preserved railway property and protected vehicles. When the ceasefire agreement was established at the end of May, the employees of the two railway lines immediately restored traffic after recovering Nanxiang, Zhenru, and North Station, achieving remarkable results, and were once again commended. During this time of national crisis, the employees risked their lives to work and fulfilled their duties, and the Ministry of Railways did its best to provide generous compensation and encouragement. Around July, the workers of the Wusong Machine Factory, feeling they had suffered losses being located in a war zone, first proposed a plan to borrow three months' salary, which was submitted to the bureau and then to the ministry. The two railway bureau chiefs, citing the precedent of the Qi-Lu War, requested the Ministry of Railways to approve the issuance of two months' bonus to the employees. The railway union also sent representatives to the ministry twice to petition. Minister of Railways Gu, considering the importance of the matter, specifically proposed it for discussion at the ministry's business meeting on October 4th. All senior officials of the ministry attended the meeting and generally believed that the January 28th Incident was a war of national resistance. All public officials in Shanghai bravely sacrificed and fulfilled their duties. Many civilians in the war zone were bankrupted, and even people near the war zone donated their homes to support the military. Therefore, the losses from this battle were widespread. Public officials in other institutions in Shanghai were not known to have received any so-called bonuses. At this time of internal and external difficulties, when the entire nation is striving to improve and be determined, if the issuance of wartime bonuses to the employees of the two railway lines is approved, it will inevitably cause misunderstandings in the outside world about the heroic sacrifices of our employees for the country. Furthermore, the finances of the two railway lines have been very strained in recent years. As of the 20th year of the Republic (1931), the Sino-British surplus profits have not been cleared for many years. The repayment of loans has been postponed for two years, and the loans for purchasing cars and land cannot be cleared. Although the bondholders have complained, there is no way to raise the funds. The total amount of due but unpaid funds has reached more than 7 million yuan. Since the Japanese invasion, reconstruction requires money everywhere. Issuing bonuses is not only legally impermissible, but also difficult due to economic constraints. However, considering that the employees' requests were sincere and the losses were real, after careful consideration, while the request for bonuses could not be approved, the suffering of the employees was taken into account, and a compromise was decided upon. "Measures for Loss Relief Loans to Employees Serving in the War Zone of the Jinghu and Huhangyong Railway Lines" were decided. The regulations stipulated that employees of the two railway lines serving within the war zone whose salaries were below 50 yuan were allowed to borrow two months' salary, those with salaries from 51 yuan to 100 yuan were allowed to borrow one and a half months' salary, and those with salaries from 101 yuan to 200 yuan were allowed to borrow one month's salary. In the future, one-tenth of their original salary would be deducted monthly. If the funds of the railway lines were insufficient, they were allowed to borrow from banks to issue the loans. The administrative bureaus of the two railway lines and the councils of the two railway line unions and employees were ordered to comply. This measure can be said to be the Ministry of Railways' attempt to provide relief in a situation where there was no other way, and it has taken great care to relieve the difficulties of lower-level employees in the war zones of the two railway lines. In addition to the above-mentioned measures for relief loans to employees serving in the war zone, the administrative bureaus of the two railway lines failed to immediately implement them, resulting in senior officials and employees from non-war zones following suit and requesting loans for all employees for two months. The administrative bureaus of the two railway lines also successively sent telegrams on behalf of the employees. The Ministry of Railways considered that the above-mentioned measures were originally intended to meet the urgent needs of lower-level employees in the war zone who had suffered losses in the Shanghai war. During the war, the salaries of the employees of the two railway lines were paid as usual, which was already a special privilege compared to other institutions. Senior officials have relatively sufficient means of support and can easily find ways to manage their finances. Furthermore, since not all areas along the two railway lines are war zones, the situation is different, so it is not appropriate to approve loans across the board. Regardless, the employees of the two railway lines who died in service have been given generous compensation, and those who contributed to protecting trains have been given special awards. From the perspective of civil servants, should they not all possess the spirit of loyalty, courage, and diligence, and the inherent duty of conscientiously performing their duties? If all employees of the two railway lines, regardless of whether they are in war zones or non-war zones, whether they have suffered losses or not, request loans, it would not only provide outsiders with grounds for criticism, but also make it impossible to justify oneself to the affected employees. Therefore, although the Ministry of Railways has the heart to care for all employees, it cannot but comprehensively plan, weigh the importance of things, and avoid further burdening the railway lines with debt. However, the employees of the two railway lines do not seem to understand this, and the administrative bureaus of the two railway lines do not seem to be able to sincerely persuade the employees, resulting in the unfortunate incident of gatherings and detentions of trains that occurred a few days ago. According to sources from the Ministry of Railways, the decision is to maintain the original plan and send personnel to sincerely explain the situation. Now, the majority of employees have understood the original intention of the Ministry of Railways in approving the loan. The Ministry of Railways is also trying to make all employees of the two railway lines fully understand the Ministry's intention to maintain the railway administration and care for the employees. The Japanese invasion is a national crisis and a great shame and humiliation that has pained our nation. The entire nation is working hard to improve and be determined, tightening their belts to wipe out the humiliation. Railway employees, being loyal and devoted to the country, should be able to overcome the difficulties of the times (uphold the overall situation and maintain the railway administration), etc.

Measures for Exchanging Silk Public Bonds 119

The 3 million yuan of Jiangzhe Silk Public Bonds has already begun to be issued. The two committees for the sorting and promotion of old silk and cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have jointly established a joint office located inside the Silk and Cocoon General Association on Beishan West Road, which was declared established on the 16th. It is determined that the silk public bonds will be subject to the first lottery for repayment of principal at the end of this month. Therefore, manufacturers holding export certificates issued by the Jianghai Customs and measurement certificates from the Raw Silk Inspection Institute should apply to the office for public bond certificates. Those that have already been sold but not yet loaded on the wheel and old factory silk currently stored in foreign firms should also request the foreign firms to load and export them before the 25th and send them to the inspection institute for examination so as to exchange export certificates and measurement certificates for public bond certificates and avoid losing the right to the first lottery for repayment of principal. Therefore, the market mistakenly believed that foreign firms had a large number of factory transactions. In fact, the silk stored in the foreign firms' warehouses was being sent for inspection and measurement in order to be loaded and exported. The chairman of the sorting committee, Zhu Jing'an, the chief of general affairs, Shen Huachen, and the chairman of the promotion committee, He Bingxian, are stationed in the office every day to work, and they are quite busy. Silk merchants applying for public bond certificates must first submit the export certificates and measurement certificates to He Bingxian, chairman of the promotion committee, for verification, and then send them upstairs to Zhu Jing'an, chairman of the sorting committee, and Chief Shen for signature and sealing, and then issue the public bond certificates, which can be used to exchange for public bond tickets from the fund management committee.

Recent News from the Municipal Zoo 124

Equipment Construction Will Be Completed Soon; Opening on New Year's Day

The Municipal Zoo on Wenmiao Road in this city, which began construction in August of this year, has now completed the second phase of equipment construction and is scheduled to open on New Year's Day. The details are recorded as follows:

Construction Progress 125

The first phase of the park's construction project was put out to tender by the Municipal Bureau of Education in August of this year and was won by Sansen Construction Company for 13,400 yuan. Since construction began, it was completed last month, and the second phase of equipment construction, including the installation of water heaters, water pipes, electric lights, and the construction of revetments, the stacking of artificial mountains, the laying of grass, and the planting of trees, has largely been completed. It will be completed within this year, and it will be opened on New Year's Day.

Arrangements 126

The park has one main gate and one side gate, facing the Municipal Education Center. It is surrounded by short walls. The office is in the center of the park. Around it is a stone-built ditch two zhang deep, for raising waterfowl. Next to it is an artificial mountain with a pavilion on top for visitors to rest. Below it is a goldfish pond and a rabbit hole. There are four animal rooms, large and small. The large ones have an area of 14 square zhang. The roof and front are all iron fences. The inner rooms are divided into two parts, currently housing a pair of newly arrived lions and a pair of black bears. There is also a room with the same area, divided into six small rooms inside and outside, with doors for passage, equipped with water heaters. During the day, animals can be driven into the outer cages for public viewing, and at night they can be housed in the inner cages to maintain body temperature. The other two rooms are smaller and are specifically used for raising tame animals. In addition, there are three thatched pavilions, surrounded by iron nets, specifically for raising birds.

Animals on Display 127

In addition to all the birds and beasts of the First School Park, there are tigers, leopards, kangaroos, lizards, partridges, etc., which are currently temporarily housed in the school park. Recently, a pair of lions was purchased from Hong Kong for 2,150 yuan, and a pair of black bears for 140 yuan, which were transported here the day before yesterday and are currently displayed in the largest animal room in the park.

News from the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Administration 129

Zhou Xiangkui, acting director of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Marine Fisheries Administration of the Ministry of Industry, received an order from the ministry to consolidate the temporary offices in various locations in the Jiangsu-Zhejiang area in order to facilitate management and rectification. After investigation, the offices in Wenningxiangnan and other places in Zhejiang were all abolished and merged into the Taizhou district office, which will manage the patrol boats under its jurisdiction. Cai Gengnan, director of the Taizhou district, will take over the command. The Zhenhai district will belong to the Dinghai district, and the patrol boats of each team will also be dispatched by the director. In Jiangsu, the offices in Songhu and Tongzhou, which were originally established, are also abolished at the same time and taken over by Zhu Songzhou, director of the Haizhou district office. Due to the rampant piracy on the coastal waters, there have been incidents of looting ships and kidnapping people, which has greatly harmed merchant ships. In order to effectively maintain maritime security, Captain Zhu quickly concentrated the fishing protection team ships to be ready for dispatch and patrol.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Again Requests Correction of the Shipping Tax in this City 130

Matters related to law and jurisdiction, violation of tax law, and should be ordered to stop immediately The Municipal Chamber of Commerce presented to the Executive Yuan and the Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday, stating: "It is submitted for presentation. On the 15th of this month, we received a letter from the barge transportation industry association in this city stating that the collection of ship registration tax by the Maritime Affairs Bureau in November of this year is actually a heavy collection agency similar to likin. We once again request that the Central Party Headquarters submit the report to the Third Plenary Session for lawful correction and cancellation of the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau, a redundant and heavily collected agency, which must not invade inland rivers to establish registration offices, which will increase the burden on lighterage merchants, delineate the functions and powers of the central and local maritime affairs agencies, and avoid obstacles to local maritime affairs agencies. The various exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous goods should be abolished and changed to a unified ship tax to unify and comply with the law," etc. Article 1 of the Ship Registration Law states, "The term 'ship' in this law refers to ships that navigate at sea and on waters that are connected to the sea and can be used by seagoing ships, as stipulated in the Maritime Law." According to this provision, in places that are not coastal or connected to the sea, there are no ships that can be used by seagoing ships. The Maritime Affairs Bureau has no place to exercise its powers in accordance with Article 2 of the Ship Registration Law, and it should not set up branches everywhere, causing chaos. This is a limitation of territorial jurisdiction. Even in coastal or connected places, for ships that can be used by seagoing ships but whose gross tonnage is less than 20 tons or whose capacity is less than 200 dan, this law does not apply. The same applies to ships whose main mode of operation is by eaves oars, which cannot be used by seagoing ships at all. In other words, they are not within the scope of registration with the Maritime Affairs Bureau. Now, the Maritime Affairs Bureau has set up branches everywhere in places that are not connected to the sea (such as Wuxi), and has forced farmers' ships and shipping ships to register and pay fees (such as Changshu), which is truly an excessive burden on merchants and violates laws and regulations. The Ministry of Transportation's reply has also failed to strictly correct the situation in accordance with the law. This matter is related to the interpretation of the law, the division of powers between the ministry and the city, and the crux of the matter is that the illegal burden on merchants is beyond their capacity to bear. Therefore, we respectfully request your court and government to examine and approve and order correction, which is in the public interest.

Planning to Dredge the Yingdou River 131

The Yingdou River originates in Jiangyin and flows into the Huangpu River. In the eastern part of the first district of Shanghai County and at the junction with the second district, it is one of the most important trunk rivers in the county, as recorded in the gazetteer. It has been more than 60 years since it was dredged during the Tongzhi period of the Qing Dynasty. In recent years, the siltation has become increasingly severe. Not only is the tide blocked, but it has even turned into flat land. The first district office and the second district office convened a meeting and decided to dredge it. A preparatory committee has been established and is actively proceeding. Wu Shifang, the chief of the first district of Shanghai County, Peng Yinqiao, the chief of the second district, Jiang Zhujun, the director of the Public Property Office, and the heads of each Zou town related to the Yingdou River are ex officio committee members, and local people who are familiar with the river and enthusiastic about public welfare are also hoped to be river committee members. A standing committee of three members is established, and the director of the Public Property Office and the chiefs of the two districts are publicly recommended by the conference as standing committee members. Jiang Zhujun is mutually elected by the standing committee members as the chairman of the committee. The regulations have been drawn up and reported to the county government for record.
