Shen Bao Medical Weekly

Inaugural Address 197

— The Editor

The purpose of publishing the Medical Weekly in this newspaper is threefold.

Humans cannot avoid illness. When illness strikes, one naturally seeks a swift recovery. This basic knowledge of medicine and pharmaceuticals is indispensable in life. This is the first reason.

With the advancement of science, various academic disciplines are constantly evolving and progressing with the times. Medicine and pharmaceuticals are no exception. Having been born in the twentieth century, it is imperative that we have at least a basic understanding of modern medicine and its trends. This is the second reason.

Medicine is a specialized academic discipline, and indeed, one of the most important academic disciplines in the world. Its relationship with the public is profound and intimate. Specialized academic disciplines must also strive for universalization, allowing more people to study them, progressing from the simple to the profound, specializing in their field, or at least grasping the main points, reconciling diverse opinions. This is the third reason.

In recent times, human affairs have become increasingly complex, and the opportunities for illness have also increased. It is imperative to understand how to prevent illness, how to avoid illness, how to seek a swift recovery, how to seek medical care, and how to seek medication. This publication will pay particular attention to these issues, allowing scholars to fully utilize their abilities and the people to achieve longevity. We have specially commissioned experts to write articles, publishing them periodically. We hope that readers will find them useful. Please start reading from today.

A Bird's-Eye View of Medicine and Pharmaceuticals in Shanghai in the Last Decade 198

— Pang Jingzhou

Table of Contents

1. Introduction

2. The Situation of Academic Theories

3. Charts and Explanations

4. The Situation of Business Operations

5. The Situation of Medical Administration

6. Conclusion

(1) Introduction

Shanghai is a large city with thriving commerce and a large population. It is not only the premier city of China but also a famous city in East Asia. Illness is inevitable in life, and medicine and pharmaceuticals are daily necessities. Therefore, it is worth discussing them. The significance of this article published to society is to seek a definite understanding of medicine and pharmaceuticals in Shanghai among the general public, so that they can work together to improve them. Extending this to the whole country, Shanghai can serve as a model. However, before entering the main text, there are several declarations:

(A) The author is a "new doctor" (commonly known as a Western doctor) and naturally speaks from a scientific standpoint. However, he does not attack "old doctors" (commonly known as Chinese doctors or national doctors). If people with "anti-scientific tendencies" are angered by this, then so be it. The metaphors and analogies in the text are intended to be clear and engaging and do not carry any intention of disrespect. Honest advice is unpleasant to the ear, and readers should understand my good intentions.

(B) The author has very little resentment toward colleagues. However, by nature, I do not seek personal gain, and my statements are inevitably straightforward. This article does not target any particular group. All the records in the text are based on verifiable facts and are not fabricated.

(C) In addition to practicing medicine in Shanghai, the author has always been fond of managing the public affairs of groups, such as medical associations, medical schools, and hospitals. Therefore, I believe that I have a relatively comprehensive understanding of the relationship between society and medicine and pharmaceuticals. Therefore, the topic is called a "bird's-eye view," but there is no arrogance or intention to look down on everything.

(D) The author has only been practicing medicine for twelve years, so I only discuss the situation in the last decade. Coincidentally, the past decade has been the most bizarre in the medical and pharmaceutical fields. Although the article discusses both medicine and pharmaceuticals, I dare not discuss the medical field too much and still maintain the attitude of a semi-outsider.

(E) For the sake of clarity, a page of geometric charts is included in the text (see below). If readers carefully read it, they can get a bird's-eye view of medicine and pharmaceuticals in Shanghai.

(F) Although this article discusses medicine and pharmaceuticals in general, it also appropriately separates them into categories: (1) the situation of medical and pharmaceutical theories, (2) the situation of medical and pharmaceutical business operations, (3) the situation of medical and pharmaceutical politics, and (4) the conclusion.

(G) Although this article is published in the Shen Bao, it is my personal opinion and does not represent the views of the Shen Bao. The author is responsible for everything.

(2) The Situation of Academic Theories (The Dispute Between New and Old Medicine) New medicine entered China initially through foreign missionaries. At that time, foreign medicine was not very developed. The number of Western doctors in China was very small and could be said to be merely decorative. Therefore, there was no dispute between new and old medicine. Since various countries have greatly promoted medicine in the past fifty years and have indeed made inventions that benefit the world, coupled with the return of batches of students studying abroad, new knowledge has been continuously imported. China's political system is reforming day by day. Therefore, the dispute between new and old theories is inevitable, especially in the past decade. In fact, society needs to recognize that the awakening of old medicine by new medicine is stimulated by the global scientific trend. It is definitely not a matter of a few people engaging in factionalism and seeking their own livelihood. Furthermore, other academic theories, such as politics, law, economics, architecture, and engineering, all gladly improve following new trends, without dissent. Why is medicine an exception? It is incomprehensible. In my personal opinion, this is probably because our country has very little emphasis on the word "medicine" and rarely promotes it, mixing it with divination, astrology, and physiognomy. Because it is not valued by the rulers, it has caused civil disputes.

The point of contention between new and old medicine is the diagnosis of diseases, not the medicines used to treat them. I am afraid that many people in society still swallow everything whole, only seeing it as you competing for business. You must know that medicines are originally herbs, tree bark, minerals, and salts. There is originally no distinction between Chinese and foreign. They can all be used. Moreover, Chinese medicines are rich in treasures, and new medicine has never completely rejected them and has even engaged in research, with many successful cases, such as ephedra and angelica. However, because domestic science is underdeveloped, these things are all done by foreigners, encroaching on others' territory. Now angelica is exported in large quantities every year, but I hear that Germany is already planting it. Perhaps in a few years, Chinese pharmacies will inevitably import German angelica that is fat and good. Old doctors must say that Chinese medicines must be used with the diagnosis of yin and yang, the five elements, and the six qi to be effective. That is what new doctors cannot admit. (And the criticism of new doctors is still based on how Western doctors were fifty years ago compared to current Western doctors. How can the two sides not argue?) In the future, our medicinal specialties will inevitably be plundered by foreigners, except for those "the meaning is in the physician" methods of decocting gold needles, which foreigners do not want.

The defense of old doctors still stands on the argument of preserving Chinese medicine. What about advocating national goods and plugging loopholes? These are all one-sided statements. If you check the customs records, you can know how much Western ginseng, cloves, borneol, and Western bezoar are imported each year and how much medicine new doctors use. Taking the entire city of Shanghai as an example, there is at least one Chinese pharmacy and one pawnshop at every bustling alley entrance, one showing the high sales of Chinese medicine and the other showing economic backwardness. As for researching Chinese medicine and improving medicinal production, it is originally the business of chemists, pharmacologists, and botanists. If you organize it according to the old method, you must also go to the drug-producing areas to work. It is definitely not scientific to install a row of "New Year's red lights" in front of a Chinese pharmacy and label it as "decocting medicine for customers."

Now that scientific talent is still lacking, it is very difficult to organize Chinese medicine. However, old doctors say, "We have already scientifically organized Chinese medicine." This excludes real science. Therefore, many quacks are established, insisting on putting electricity into ginseng gelatin to make some "electrified ginseng gelatin," creating an unprecedented joke.

The old ones are quite willing to innovate, and the new ones are inconvenient to restore the old. Therefore, people in society believe that the offense and defense are different, and public opinion inevitably leans toward the old. This is also human nature. However, unscrupulous people inevitably borrow the method of innovation to gain sympathy from society and implement their tricks of using both new and old methods. In fact, we know that the theories of new and old are still in a period of contention. It is definitely not a period when the techniques of new and old can be applied simultaneously. (After reading this article, perhaps you will fully understand the loud calls of new doctors.) Ten years ago, there were only two kinds of doctors in society: new and old. The old ones had their old theories and dared not falsely claim to know the new. The new ones dared not participate in the ancient. The two were clear and did their own thing. If each had its own records and each had its own statistics, perhaps a considerable right and wrong would emerge. If we do not compare it with countries around the world, we cannot say that China has no medicine and pharmaceuticals. In the past ten years, speculative "new and old integrations" have occurred. What is a stroke is called cerebral hemorrhage, and there are also "strokes in the meridians." Such theories are the great calamity of the people.

New medicine is based on science, and old medicine is based on metaphysics. Science requires thorough understanding, and metaphysics requires understanding that cannot be expressed in words. Modern physics and chemistry, and the yin and yang and five elements far from the I Ching, may not be able to come together for a while. I don't know how many centuries it will take to have an understanding. Therefore, it is okay for the National Medicine Museum to preserve the theories of old medicine as a kind of literature to be verified after a few centuries. To put it into practical use may not be in line with the trend. Furthermore, the research of metaphysics seems to be endless, and the end is right in front of us. (See figure for details) There is no procedure to follow. (But the purpose of running the National Medicine Museum now is different. It seems not to invite learned old doctors to organize existing records, but to shake the foundations of metaphysics and put on a scientific hat). The author has two friends. One is Mr. Wang Miaoda, who practices old medicine in Hangzhou. Presumably, old doctors admire him very much. One is his younger brother, Mr. Wang Weigen, who runs a hospital in Shaoxing. He is a new doctor who has returned from studying in Germany. Although they are brothers, they have never professed to communicate theories. However, Mr. Wang Weigen's theories can still educate others. As for Mr. Miaoda's skills, according to him, they can only be understood and cannot be expressed in words. This is a metaphor for the impracticality of metaphysics. It is also an example of learned scholars who are unwilling to force things. (To be continued)

Promoting the Popularization of Knowledge of Pathological Anatomy 199

— Yu Yunxiu

The state of human organs is different when they are healthy and when they are diseased. The internal panorama of a healthy person has already been recorded in human models and anatomical atlases, which can be found in all new-style bookstores. In addition, the physiology textbooks in secondary schools also record their outlines. Therefore, modern people can roughly understand the internal panorama of a normal healthy person (hereinafter referred to as "healthy person"). Therefore, various fallacies of the ancients, such as "the liver is on the left, the spleen is on the right," "the heart has seven orifices," and "the lungs have six lobes," can be slightly pointed out and understood, because they have already acquired this kind of common sense.

As for what the internal panorama of a sick person is like, bookstores have neither pathological atlases nor pathological models. Ordinary schools also do not have courses teaching pathology. There are no ordinary pathological textbooks to refer to. Members of society who want to know the internal panorama of a sick person have no way to glimpse its secrets. Therefore, the disease of stroke is clearly a change in the spinal cord and brain, but people in society still say that it is phlegm and heat. The disease of pulmonary tuberculosis is clearly a change in the lungs, but people in society still say that it is deficiency and evil. If the true nature of the disease is not clear, then the principles of recuperation and treatment will be uncertain, the will will not be firm, and even doctors and shamans will be employed together, and miscellaneous medicines will be thrown in randomly, resulting in loss of life and property, which is useless and harmful, and very pitiful.

Therefore, what I advocate is to take the internal changes of various important diseases and develop them into simple explanations, either publishing them in newspapers or compiling them into small pamphlets, distributing them to society, revealing the secrets of the disease nest, and revealing the truth of the abnormal state. Then the tripod of Yu will be in sight, and the monsters and demons will have nowhere to hide. Members of society can also understand where the nest of a certain disease is in which organ, and what kind of changes influence the occurrence of a certain symptom. Further, they can seek the layout of the nest and the type of abnormal state. Then the disease's ease or difficulty of treatment, as well as the treatment plan and recuperation method, can also be roughly grasped. That is, when a doctor treats a certain disease, wants to take what kind of method, and his explanation to the patient's family to seek the patient's family's understanding is also easier. In this way, the patient's family will not, until the time of total destitution when there is no way out, or will not be deceived by heresies, bewitched by external paths, and will not combine doctors and shamans, and the harm of throwing in miscellaneous medicines can also be slightly reduced. The lives and property of patients lost to the childish family's advocacy can also be slightly reduced.

Now, if we take the traditional knowledge of stroke symptoms of our country's ancients and verify them with pathological anatomy knowledge, we can correct their fallacies. The body of a person with stroke must have a bleeding disease nest in his brain when it is dissected, which can be observed. This has been verified in thousands of people and summarized in various countries in the East and West, and there is no error. Moreover, its

Page 14

bleeding disease nest is in different locations, and the external symptoms that occur are also different. Those with eye deviation have a disease nest in the posterior lobe of the cerebrum. The ancients thought that it was in the liver. Those who cannot speak (motor aphasia) have a disease nest in the frontal lobe of the cerebrum. The ancients thought that it was in the heart. Those with slack lips have facial nerve paralysis. The disease nest may be in the lower part of the central 𢌞 gyrations of the cerebrum or in the knee of the internal capsule. The ancients thought that it was in the spleen. The ancients also considered constipation to be in the spleen. Those with constipation have paralysis of the rectum. This symptom belongs to the internal nerve. This symptom is not common in stroke and is not from the same source as slack lips. All are attributed to stroke in the spleen, which is even more incorrect. The ancients also considered nasal congestion to be in the lungs. There is no symptom of nasal congestion in stroke. It is just an empty statement to fill the number of the five viscera. Those who are deaf have hearing impairment. The disease nest is at the posterior end of the posterior limb of the internal capsule. The ancients thought that it was in the kidneys. This is the ancient theory of stroke in the five viscera, and its true pathological anatomical picture is like this. Thus, anatomy, physiology, and disease condition are consistent, and the ancient theory of disease symptoms, based on the traditional knowledge of the twelve meridians, can be organized. As for hemiplegia being called stroke, but arm paralysis being called numbness, in fact, those with hemiplegia have a disease nest in the internal capsule. Those with paraplegia in both limbs or one limb alone have a disease nest mostly in the cerebral cortex. Now it is called monoplegia. Thus, the confusion of names and realities can be understood. Therefore, if the knowledge of pathology can be popularized, not only can society increase its clarity of concepts about disease, but it will also be of great benefit to the organization of figures. Further, in our country's society that values corpses, the implementation of pathological anatomy may also gradually become popular.

The Ideal Doctor in My Eyes and the Ideal Doctor in the Eyes of the Masses 200

— Wang Qizhang

The ancients said, "The best doctor treats before illness. To treat after illness is the work of a lesser doctor." I won't talk about this "best doctor" for now. Because in today's world where public health is underdeveloped, there's no point in discussing treating before illness. Here, let me talk about the "ideal doctor" in terms of treatment. On the surface, the duty of us doctors seems to be simply to treat diseases. However, there should also be a grand goal in treating diseases. It's not enough to simply copy ancient prescriptions or privately admire established methods. Nor is it enough to simply imitate Zichan's saving people from the quagmire. Even less is it enough to imitate Zaiwo's rescuing people from a well. Because diseases are not limited to what the ancients knew, especially not limited to what the ancients could treat. They are also not limited to what I know or what I can treat. Besides the diseases known and treated by the ancients and me, they can occur and spread at any time, depending on the era, location, and environment. Even based on our current observations and experiments, there is a trend of unlimited increase. Isn't it very difficult to both understand and treat these increasing diseases? Therefore, the duty of a doctor is not only to be good at treating known diseases, but also to know and treat unknown diseases. It is not only to be able to treat both known and unknown diseases, but also to improve and invent methods to deal with both known and unknown diseases. Therefore, we must never cling to established rules and ancient methods and consider ourselves satisfied or fulfilled. Haven't I said before? The fundamental concepts of ancient doctors and modern doctors are completely different. Ancient doctors emphasized conservatism, while modern doctors emphasize progress. Ancient doctors only took established methods as dogma, while modern doctors often take established methods as a reference. Ancient doctors valued ideals and empty talk, deducing medical principles and matching them with symptoms. Modern doctors use scientific substances to eliminate pathogens and treat diseases. Therefore, their trends, directions, and business operations often run counter to each other. Of course, there is no possibility of consistent cooperation. Today's social disorder and occupational complexity can be said to have reached their peak. The levels of scholarship and the classes of knowledge are often separated by two or three thousand years. Therefore, it is inevitable that the minds of each person cannot be focused on one line. We, as doctors who inevitably bear the mark of the times, in this era, as people of this era, treating patients of this era, should use methods that are also in line with the modern era, and use medicines that are also relevant to the modern era. Because past medicines are already outdated, just like us doctors bearing the mark of the times, we will inevitably not fit into the future. Therefore, the doctors who can be called "ideal doctors" in our eyes today are roughly limited to the following levels. The first-rate ideal doctor is a person who can eradicate one or several major human enemies. The second-rate ideal doctor is a person who can improve ancient methods to treat known diseases and discover new methods to treat unknown diseases. The third-rate ideal doctor is a person who can happily use established methods to cope with diseases. As for those demons who know only half of what they should and treat the precious human body as a drug testing ground, they cannot be considered doctors. Of course, they cannot dream of the word "ideal." And even the word "mediocre" is still difficult to hope for. Because "mediocre" means ordinary, and "mediocre" also means not easily changing. The so-called mediocre and insignificant people neither benefit nor harm diseases. For the sake of maintaining their reputation, status, and livelihood, they simply prescribe a few lightly described decoctions. Although everyone praises them as famous doctors, they are actually mediocre doctors who live up to their name. They can never kill people, nor can they save people. In the end, they only mislead people. These are my views on what an ideal doctor is.

Now, let me say a few words about the "ideal doctor" in the eyes of the masses. Didn't I say earlier? In today's society, the levels of scholarship and the classes of knowledge are separated by two or three thousand years. Of course, it is extremely difficult for psychology to be consistent. As for how much? About one-thousandth is modern, ten-thousandths is near modern, twenty-thousandths is skeptical, and the rest are all ancient minds. (I dare not say that the distribution of medical knowledge is appropriate.) Therefore, people with ancient minds must be paired with ancient knowledge in order to be compatible. In our current society, most aspects of materials are new. Especially in terms of knowledge and medicine, most are old. Therefore, medicine from two thousand years ago is most in line with the psychology of our current society and most welcomed by the public in current society. And this belief is not the actual result, but a kind of illusion in knowledge and psychology. Therefore, the ideal doctor in the eyes of society must of course be pursued from this aspect. On the one hand, in addition to people in the modern knowledge class, plus the near-modern and skeptical parts, they are also inevitably affected by my faults. They will bury the facts of medicine in hearsay. Not to mention the public who have no ability to discern, they will fall into their trap. Even people with judgmental abilities often get confused and cannot tell right from wrong. There are also quite a few. So the two words "ideal doctor" are even more difficult to say. However, doctors who are keen on pursuing profits seize this good opportunity and go straight in. They know that the social custom of worshiping writing has not changed, so they take advantage of the opportunity to use their writing to attract patients. They also know the principle that no one can be an official without someone in the court, and no one can be a doctor without someone in the city. In addition to not offending the powerful families, they work hard to win over the wealthy and befriend the powerful. They use them to indirectly attract patients. They also know the greatness of the money demon and the moving nature of the name of charity, so they pretend to be charitable and make a small hole in their wallets to indirectly attract patients. These techniques are all medicine outside of medical skills. His attraction is extremely powerful. After a few years, he won a market like a city, and the praise never stopped. Therefore, the ideal doctor who takes the number of patients as a standard is an ideal doctor who is a kind of illusion in the knowledge and psychology of a group of people in society. It is not the ideal doctor in our eyes. It is the ideal doctor obtained from the results of medicine outside of medical skills. It is not the several kinds of academic ideal doctors that we mentioned above. Furthermore, the doctor that a group of people in society mistakenly believe to be an ideal doctor, the more patients he attracts, the lighter and more perfunctory his medical duties become. Because he is desperate to keep his job. He does not seek merit for diseases, but only seeks no fault. Therefore, his prescriptions only win everyone's praise for being stable. He will then escape the relationship of misleading people's lives. Furthermore, he has many patients, but his energy is limited. He needs to calculate the time and increase his income for medical treatment and prescriptions. Therefore, patients who have been waiting for a long time only need to get the doctor, touch his pulse, and prescribe his prescription to be satisfied. They don't even ask if the prescription is right or if the medicine is effective. There is also the general social psychology, if it is not the ideal doctor in their eyes, if they prescribe a prescription and take a medicine, there are still many criticisms and accusations. When it comes to their so-called ideal doctor, even if there is an error and they lose the lives of their family members, they not only do not have a single word of complaint, but also wholeheartedly defend them. They say that it was treated by a certain ideal doctor and it could not be cured. It's really called a fatal illness. There's no way. No one has even gone to study the patient's illness and the prescriptions they prescribed and the medicines they used! Alas! Do you think it's pathetic? But now, there are still many of these ideal doctors, and they are still constantly appearing. Is it a good phenomenon? Or a bad phenomenon? Let's wait until the majority of the public puts their brains in fast gear and catches up to two thousand years before we can start talking. Otherwise, we can only listen to the noisy cicadas in the dark and murky night.

On Treatment 201

— Yugong

The common mentality is that doctors rely solely on pulse diagnosis and prescriptions to treat diseases. If the disease is cured, the credit is attributed to the medicine. If it is not cured, the blame is attributed to the medicine. It is as if there is no other way to treat diseases besides medicine. When a doctor examines a patient, if he does not prescribe a prescription, it will cause misunderstandings among the patients. Some think that the doctor lacks sufficient knowledge, and others think that the disease is not easy to treat. All kinds of speculations are endless. Furthermore, they even have doubts about the entire medical community, so that the concept that Western medicine is good at surgery and short in internal medicine is deeply rooted in people's hearts. This is indeed a major obstacle to the promotion of new medicine.

In fact, there are many ways to treat diseases. The first thing to do is to make an accurate diagnosis, and then there should be reasonable treatment. The so-called reasonable treatment is to apply the methods that scientists have researched and applied to treat the disease. At first, it is not limited to medicine. Let's cite a few examples to illustrate this.

(1) Rest Therapy: When a person is unfortunately ill, the first thing to pay attention to is to maintain physical strength and not waste it at all in order to increase resistance, drive away the disease, and restore health. The principle is very obvious. Those who suffer from typhoid fever or pneumonia must lie down extremely quietly until the body temperature returns to normal for ten days before they can get out of bed. Those who suffer from influenza should also lie down quietly for at least two days. Those who suffer from tuberculosis, if they have chills and fever, should absolutely rest quietly in bed. Wait until the fever subsides, two or three weeks before they can get out of bed. When the fever recurs, they must lie down quietly again. This kind of rest treatment is amazingly effective. But the common mentality is that being sick in bed is not a good sign. Therefore, even if they have chills and fever, they still force themselves to sit up. Until not only the original symptoms are not relieved, but also complications occur one after another. Being ignorant of the early signs, they often fall into incurable situations. The importance of this rest treatment cannot but be paid attention to.

(2) Dietary Treatment: Dietary treatment is very important in various diseases. For example, in the treatment of diabetes, the daily diet must be carefully weighed, properly controlled, and qualitatively regular. It should be determined according to the patient's daily situation. The amount of "carbohydrates" and "proteins" given is based on the premise that the urine does not contain sugar, and the amount of "fat" must ensure that the patient does not have ketoacidosis. Those who suffer from acute nephritis must be given a light diet and avoid foods containing "protein." Those who suffer from beriberi, the main treatment is to correct the lack of "vitamins" in their food. Those who suffer from rickets must have "vitamin A" in their food. As for other diseases, there are those who use liquid food, gruel food, nourishing food, or solid food, which vary according to the disease. If someone suffers from acute gastritis, they often do not allow food except water for a long time in order to give the gastric mucosa a proper rest. This dietary treatment cannot be ignored.

(3) Cold or Heat Treatment: The application of external cold or heat also has a very important impact on the disease. For example, those who suffer from acute nephritis often use hot wet cloths to wrap the body to make the patient sweat, so that the toxins in the body that cannot be excreted through the urinary tract can be excreted through sweat. Those who suffer from typhoid fever or pneumonia, place ice on the forehead. Those who suffer from laryngitis, place it on the neck. Those who suffer from gastric ulcers and bleeding, place it on the upper part of the abdomen, and those who suffer from heatstroke even need to immerse the whole body in ice water and then wipe it with a damp towel until the body temperature drops to 101 degrees. The application of cold and heat varies according to the disease. Not only does it reduce the symptoms, but it also has the effect of saving lives. How can we ignore it? (4) Surgical Treatment: Surgical treatment methods vary. Everyone knows about surgery and injections. However, surgery is not limited to knives and injections. There are artificial respiration surgery, bloodletting surgery, and blood transfusion surgery. Artificial respiration is widely used. For example, in cases of gas poisoning, morphine poisoning, anesthetic poisoning, and carbon monoxide poisoning, it can often bring the dead back to life. Bloodletting surgery is used for acute heart failure. It can reduce the expansion of capillaries in the lungs. Blood transfusion surgery can be used for excessive bleeding, carbon monoxide poisoning, and chronic anemia. (To be continued)

Using Traditional Chinese Medicine with a Western Approach 202

— Zhou Mengbai

Traditional Chinese medicine has theories about cold, heat, warmth, coolness, rising, lowering, floating, and sinking. These all come from conforming to fallacies such as yin and yang and the five elements. However, the effect of treating diseases cannot be denied. For example, Pinellia ternata suppresses vomiting, Ephedra sinica induces sweating, apricot kernels treat coughs, and rhubarb induces diarrhea. These are all real achievements. As for how they can suppress vomiting, induce sweating, treat coughs, and induce diarrhea, they are all unknown. This is knowing that it is so, but not knowing why it is so. Now, if we want to know why it is so, we must use scientific sorting and research. For example, use botany to recognize its genus, use pharmacognosy to identify its quality, use chemistry to analyze its properties, use pharmacology to test its efficacy, and make a systematic report. Doctors then use it in clinical practice. In this way, not only can the original efficacy be verified, but new effects are often discovered. However, this sorting and research work cannot be done without sufficient funding and new medical talents who are familiar with research, and it takes a considerable amount of time. It is not like a crudely made, nonsensical mixed medicine, conforming to a little medical knowledge that is still under research and discussion, and using advertising techniques like telling fairy tales to tell the public: "This is a special medicine for a certain disease." This is a new medicine that has been scientifically improved. It is like the medicines sold on the market recently that are not produced by pharmacists, deceiving themselves and others. It is truly a pest in the scientific community and a scourge in the medical community. Now, in order to provide something for drug manufacturers to follow and something for drug users to have a standard, I will excerpt here traditional Chinese medicines that have been sorted and researched, whose properties have been clearly understood, and whose effects have been verified, all of which have been achieved through academic theory and have been included in the Pharmacopoeia of the People's Republic of China. This may increase the general public's medical common sense, so that they can make choices when consulting doctors and purchasing medicines. However, there may be something wrong with what I say. I hope that my medical colleagues can come forward and teach me. (To be continued)

Economic Special

On the Government's Urgent Need to Help the Cotton Industry 203

— Mu Ouchu

The cotton industry is China's largest industry. The capital of Chinese-owned factories alone is as high as 150 million yuan. It employs hundreds of thousands of workers. The number of merchants engaged in the transportation of cotton yarn and cloth is even greater. It is also the most powerful tool to resist foreign goods. The import of foreign goods into China is mainly cotton goods. If China's cotton production increases by one part, the import of foreign goods can be reduced by one part. Since the government changed the unified tax on cotton yarn, the annual fiscal revenue should be more than 20 million yuan. The importance of China's cotton industry in the national economy and national finance should be valued by the people.

Since the cotton industry is as important as described above in relation to the national economy and national finance, the prosperity or decline of the cotton industry is not only a matter of interest to the cotton industry itself. The national finance and the national economy are also affected. I have been serving the cotton industry for nearly 20 years. I not only feel the great responsibility, but also have to fully expose the various weaknesses of the cotton industry in order to ask the government and the people to pay attention. Because the cotton industry is under heavy pressure from international competition, all kinds of weaknesses have been followed for a long time and are difficult to reverse. Without government assistance, the cotton industry itself cannot solve them. Now, based on my experience, I will list the various weaknesses of the cotton industry as follows:

(1) Insufficient raw cotton: China's cotton exports have always been one of the major native products. In recent years, with the increasing number of yarn factories, the demand for raw cotton has increased day by day. The output of domestic cotton is not enough to supply the needs of the factories, so American cotton and Indian cotton have been imported in large quantities. In 1930, the total import of foreign cotton reached 170 million customs taels, equivalent to more than 260 million yuan in national currency. In 1931, the total import of foreign cotton was also 130 million customs taels, equivalent to more than 200 million yuan in national currency. This is one of the shortcomings of China's cotton industry.

(2) Poor cotton quality: Not only is China's cotton production too small, but most of it is of poor quality and is not suitable for spinning fine yarn. In recent years, although good American varieties have been imported as much as possible, because Chinese cotton farmers lack knowledge and do not know how to select good varieties, the original American varieties with longer fibers have gradually degraded and become coarse after several years. As a result, those who spin fine yarn and double-strand thread still have to use American cotton as raw material. Therefore, there are many who have failed due to the high exchange rate of foreign countries. This is the second shortcoming of China's cotton industry.

(3) Deep-rooted Malpractices: China's cotton market has no fixed standards. Those who sell cotton often mix inferior cotton with good cotton. What's more, they add moisture and water to increase the weight and seek improper benefits. Watered cotton often rots in early summer, causing the yarn factory to suffer a lot of invisible losses. This is the third shortcoming of China's cotton industry.

(4) Cotton Theft and Leakage: Cotton in the interior of China is transported to major trading ports. The distant ones are thousands of miles away, and the nearby ones are also hundreds of miles away. The theft and loss along the way are also huge. Loose packages are common. Even machine-packed, so-called foreign frames, also have theft and leakage. This increases the cost of cotton. This is the fourth shortcoming of China's cotton industry.

(5) Immature Textile Technology: China's cotton textile industry is relatively late compared with other countries. In recent years, there has been progress in technology compared with the past. However, compared with Japanese-owned factories, it is still inferior. This is the fifth shortcoming of China's cotton industry.

(6) Difficult to Manage Workers: Because Chinese workers lack knowledge, their original work ability is not as good as others. In addition, in recent years, trends have led to disputes. There are even those who do not work but specialize in inciting trends as a skill. Factories are almost at a loss for management difficulties. This is the sixth shortcoming of China's cotton industry.

(7) Weak Work Ability: Chinese yarn factories employ far more workers than Japanese-owned factories. Japanese yarn factories use about 240 workers per 10,000 spindles for spinning 20-count yarn. Chinese yarn factories use at least 350 workers per 10,000 spindles for spinning 20-count yarn, and as many as 750 workers. Because there are no labor unions in Japanese factories, workers are trained and have higher skills, while Chinese factories are not. This is the seventh shortcoming of China's cotton industry.

(8) Lower Production Volume: According to a survey in 1925, the average output per spindle of 20-count yarn in Japanese factories was 0.434 pounds per ten hours. If calculated according to 24 hours a day, the output of 20-count yarn per spindle is more than one pound. At the same time, the average output per spindle of 20-count yarn in Chinese factories is about 0.7 pounds per 24 hours, which is one-third less. This is the eighth shortcoming of China's cotton industry.

(9) Higher Labor Costs: Because of the above reasons, the labor costs of Chinese factories are higher than those of Japanese factories. Therefore, even if Japanese factories sell at a slightly lower price, they can still make a profit. Moreover, in normal times, the yarn from Japanese factories is of better quality, and the selling price is often higher than the yarn from Chinese factories. Under the same conditions, it is difficult for Chinese factories to compete with Japanese factories. This is the ninth shortcoming of China's cotton industry.

Based on raw materials, technology, and labor costs, it is already difficult for China's cotton industry to compete with Japanese factories. However, China's cotton industry still has other shortcomings in finance, transportation, and other aspects.

(1) Lack of Public Reserves: Japanese-owned factories in China are all branch factories. Their annual operating profits have huge public reserves. In total, all public reserves are more than one times the capital. Therefore, they are deeply rooted. Most Chinese-owned factories have no public reserves, or even if they do, the amount is not huge.

(2) Weak Capital: Chinese-owned factories often have businesses that are larger than their capital. Financial turnover is extremely difficult.

(3) Excessive Interest Rates: Because of the lack of working capital, they have to borrow from banks and money shops. The monthly interest rate is often more than one percent, and some are as high as 1.4 or 5 percent per month. It is really unbearable.

(4) Slow Transportation: Japanese merchants have special agreements with Japanese shipping companies for transporting American and Indian cotton, giving priority to loading. Even when selling yarn and cloth in various parts of China, Japanese commercial ships will load them as quickly as possible. Chinese-owned factories not only have no foreign shipping industry, but also have many obstacles in domestic transportation. They are far inferior to Japanese merchants in transportation.

(5) Heavy Taxes: Japanese merchants' purchase of cotton and sale of yarn are protected by treaties. After one tax, they can travel throughout the country. However, Chinese-owned factories cannot enjoy this benefit. The excessive taxes in the interior of the country still exist. (6) Inland Yarn Factories are at the Mercy of Others: In major trading ports, there are many factories, and many of them are established by foreign merchants. There are more accidents. As for the factories in the interior, because of inconvenient transportation and lack of information, they often suffer unexpected damage and cannot appeal.

(7) Yarn Factory Authorities Have Short-sighted Vision and Cannot Consolidate Groups: Japan's cotton textile industry has a strong group. They use their full power to oppress China's cotton industry and attack China's cotton industry. They want to monopolize the Chinese market with Japan's cotton industry. For several years, they have been making progress. The import of Japanese cotton goods into China has accounted for the first place of China's imported goods. Japanese-owned factories in China are in a superior position compared to Chinese-owned factories. However, the authorities of Chinese factories still cannot consolidate groups to resist foreign aggression. This is also one of the major reasons why Chinese cotton cannot be developed.

The cotton industry is in a very important position for the national economy and national finance. However, its own shortcomings are as described above. For the present plan, we cannot but hope that the government will actively help. The two most important things are:

(1) Increase Import Tariffs on Cotton Goods: Japan is the largest importer of cotton goods in China. Because of the Sino-Japanese Tariff Mutual Benefit Agreement in 1930, we cannot freely increase taxes. However, the agreement will expire on May 6, 1933, which is less than five months away. We sincerely hope that the government will pay attention to this as soon as possible and prepare in advance. Once the agreement expires, we will announce the specific measures to increase taxes on imported cotton goods to protect the domestic cotton industry.

(2) Actively Plan the Entire Plan for the Development of the Cotton Industry: China's cotton industry has shortcomings in various aspects. We must plan and establish an entire plan for the active development of the cotton industry. At the same time, we must comply and cannot solve the problems in a piecemeal way. If the government has the determination to actively develop the cotton industry, it will not worry about having no way. I am not talented, and I will continue to submit my opinions to the government.

A Brief Discussion of Modern Currency (Part 2) 204

— Translated by Ke

Chapter 2: The Standard of Currency

After long-term experience, the ancients realized that metal was the best material for making coins. Therefore, they specialized in using metal for currency. Other types of auxiliary currencies were gradually eliminated, and metal currency became the only popular one because: ㈠ Metal rotates extremely easily, and its handling is more convenient than any other material; ㈡ It is extremely durable and its quality does not deteriorate over time. Even after repeated use, its consumption is minimal; ㈢ If it is only regarded as a commodity, it has great uses in the manufacturing industry, so everyone is happy to obtain it; ㈣ It has luster and brilliance, and can be used as ornaments, which increases its value; ㈤ It is easy to split, and can be made into units of any size for use; Finally, the quantity of metal is relatively small, but not too small. Compared with daily necessities, its scarcity gives it a higher value, but it is still sufficient to meet all social needs. In short, metal possesses the six qualities of a good currency, so it is suitable to be adopted as the raw material for currency.

These six standards are still the criteria for selecting currency materials in today's laws, but in ancient times, some aspects were particularly important. First, gold, silver, and copper were scarce in ancient times, so their prices were higher. Second, these soft metals could be easily cast with relatively crude tools. In addition, gold and silver had a sacred quality in the minds of ancient people. These two materials were the most exquisite substances known to ancient people, so they were often offered to the gods they worshiped, and used to decorate their temples and Buddha statues. After this, people gradually regarded gold and silver as sacred, and their value became even higher.

Therefore, gold, silver, and copper were mostly used as currency to replace all other media of exchange among more advanced nations. However, at one time, iron was also used as currency and was popular everywhere, but it was soon eliminated. As the quantity of iron increased, its price dropped. If iron was used as currency, a large amount was required, which was cumbersome and difficult to use, so it was eventually abandoned and replaced by other more convenient materials. There are many examples of using iron as currency in history. For example, Lycurgus of Sparta decreed that iron should be the legal currency. He did this because he did not want the people of Sparta to become a commercialized people and forget their warrior spirit. Iron is very heavy, so using it as currency could reduce the people's desire to accumulate iron coins, and commerce could reduce its power to attract people to engage in it, so that the people of Sparta could concentrate on military training to create a strong military nation.

Copper also gradually lost its position as a copper coin. Today, it is often used as a subsidiary coin to pay for very small amounts only.

As the quality of currency gradually trended towards gold and silver, advanced countries also moved towards the standardization of currency. The expansion of trade made its scope, quantity, and procedures increasingly broad and complex, so it was necessary to have currency with fixed weight and price to facilitate its progress. The first things that moved in this direction and became fixed currencies seemed to be ornaments. The purpose of ancient ornaments was to decorate the body to enhance beauty, but sometimes they were also used as currency. For example, the Bible records the use of ornaments as currency. Genesis describes how Rebekah offered water to Abraham's servant and his camels, and the servant rewarded her with an earring weighing half a shekel and bracelets weighing ten shekels. This clearly shows that ornaments were also used as currency.

The transition from standardized ornaments to fixed coinage was just a matter of a hair's breadth. What is called coinage is nothing more than a fixed weight of metal containing a fixed amount of pure ingredients, with its reliability certified and imprinted by a group or a powerful person to form a fixed form of use. This certification can be done by a group of metallurgists, a group of merchants, or one or two emperors. The earliest use of coins came from Egypt and Lydia, with the latter being earlier.

The earliest coins were cast from a combination of gold and silver. This combination was called Electrum. The reason why these two metals were combined to make coins was not intentional by the coiners, but out of necessity. The ores of gold and silver were often mixed together, and there were no good metallurgists to separate them at that time, so they were used as they were, and this combined coin was formed.

The color of coins cast from gold and silver was not very pleasing, so as people's metallurgical knowledge improved, they analyzed and smelted them, and cast coins separately, while also slightly adding other base metals to increase their hardness and color.

After coins became popular, trade became much more convenient, because the value of coins was fixed, and their counting was very easy, unlike gold nuggets or other things that had to be tested, measured, and divided for use.

The use of coins is not without its drawbacks. There are many dangers involved. Counterfeiting and private minting have existed since ancient times. Even official coiners often eroded the weight and composition of coins for personal gain. Cunning people might scrape or chisel coins to extract scattered gold for profit, or use acid to extract residue from coins to enrich themselves, or rub new coins together to collect the shavings for use. Problems like these have occurred since the advent of coins, and are especially serious today. Every country has extremely strict laws to punish counterfeiters and destroyers of coins, and every country spends huge amounts of money every year to ensure the composition and weight of its currency. If this is not done, a large number of bad coins will drive all the good coins out of circulation. But in fact, this situation still often occurs. Although the prohibitions are strict, there are still many violators, and the government can do nothing about it.

The reason why bad coins drive out good coins is very simple. People always like to hoard coins with full value, and let inferior coins circulate in the market. The same is true for bankers and merchants. They must transport coins to foreign countries to pay various debts. The recipients in foreign countries will only accept these coins after they have been examined. Therefore, for the sake of credit and convenience, they must also collect good coins and transport them to foreign countries. The combination of the two makes the number of good coins circulating on the market decrease and the number of bad coins increase. Therefore, the general public, seeing the abundance of bad coins and fearing their unreliability, also compete to hoard good coins, and the amount of good coins in circulation decreases day by day.

The first person to notice this phenomenon and pay attention to it was Sir Thomas Gresham of England. Gresham was a famous English banker and merchant. Seeing this situation, he pointed it out to the public and explained its advantages and disadvantages, so the rule that bad coins drive out good coins is called Gresham's Law. This law is not only applicable in the Middle Ages, but is still useful today. However, the inferior coins in the meantime are not only coins that have been scraped or have insufficient composition.

The practice of combining two metals to make one coin is called Symmetallism. This term is often encountered in the writings of various economists, but its meaning is not very important, because the practice of combining coins has long been eliminated.

In countries with higher culture, gold and silver are often cast into two kinds of coins and used together as legal tender. This situation is called Bimetallism. The bimetallic standard has been a fiercely debated topic since the beginning of economics, and has also caused great political disputes in various countries, even today. There are countless writings on this system, and all kinds of prejudices and sophistry are attached to it. Those who hate it denounce it as the source of all economic evils, while those who like it see it as the most flexible system that can adapt to the needs of the times and places. The rights and wrongs are confusing, so it is no wonder that the general public always regards it as something they cannot understand.

However, is the bimetallic standard really something that people cannot understand? A little investigation will show that this is not the case. The system is not difficult to understand, but it is difficult to implement. A country that adopts the bimetallic standard uses both gold and silver as legal tender. People can pay debts and taxes with either one, and the two can be used interchangeably. A person who owes gold can repay it with silver, and a person who owes silver can repay it with gold. The creditor cannot refuse to accept it simply because it is a different kind.

The implementation of the bimetallic standard is regulated by law. The government designates mints, treasuries, or central banks. Anyone who wants to sell gold must be purchased with a corresponding amount of coins, and it must be guaranteed that this amount of pure gold will be sold at this price at any time. At the same time, they have the same responsibility for pure silver. Anyone who wants to sell pure silver must be purchased at a certain price, and it must be guaranteed that pure silver will be sold at the same price at any time. (To be continued)

The Atmosphere of the Financial Silver Market is Dull 205

Yesterday, the banking sector was closed for the usual Sunday holiday, and the atmosphere in the money market was sluggish. As a result, no one competed for the premium, and the result was the same price as the previous day, at seven mace, one candareen, and four li. There was no slight difference between the morning and afternoon markets. The silver exchange was over-collateralized, and the banks did not accept remittances, resulting in an unusually large amount of slippage. Both markets generally made blank loans, with the number of exchange drafts made in the morning market being 260,000 and in the afternoon market being 85,000. Only 10,000 banknotes were traded in the morning market, and there was no news of any off-market banknotes. The exchange bill transactions were also impossible to calculate due to the blank silver exchange loans. Money shops received over 5.4 million in silver dollars, and silver shops received over 21 million in silver dollars. Suspicious remittances from all routes received over 400,000, and outward remittances from customers only amounted to 40,000 to 50,000 inland. Transactions in small money shops amounted to over 600,000. In the morning market, the auxiliary currency, Jiangnan small dollars, was priced at six mace, two candareens, four li, and a half, which was two and a half li lower than the previous afternoon. The Focus of American Cotton is on the War Debt Issue 207

A telegram from New York on December 10th reported on the cotton market conditions for the week, stating that progress had been made in continuing to pay war debts, but there was no certainty about domestic rural relief programs. This week, raw cotton transactions were restricted, there were not many sellers, short positions were covered, and there was some demand from the same industry, but there were no large sales in the South. The reason for this was mostly due to a vague hope that rural relief programs might cause cotton prices to rise. Due to these factors, cotton prices rebounded, but the cotton market showed signs of a looser position in the future compared to before. France's failure to pay its debt may have triggered some selling pressure, but at the same time, there was a clear hope that a re-examination of the entire war debt issue could have a revitalizing impact on world commerce. The House Agriculture Committee is currently hearing debates on rural relief war debt programs that have automatic domestic allocation plans. The experimental measures contained in this bill are currently subject to criticism, but Congress believes that, in any case, a rural relief program is essential.

Free Talk

Short Story

On a Riverboat (3) 220

— Serving the Buddha

"Something strange has happened on the boat; please come with me to investigate." "Have you lost something?" the uniformed officer asked.

"No; I fear something involving a life. I'm confident my judgment is correct. Please come and take a look with me."

The officer stood up in surprise, looking at the old man doubtfully. The old man continued:

"Please call for a few more people, preferably with handguns or something similar. This matter won't be easy to handle." The officer dared not decide on his own and went to see the captain, recounting the matter. The captain didn't quite believe it and questioned the old man carefully. The old man didn't answer much, only saying, "Hurry up, the boat is about to reach the dock, you will be responsible for this."

The captain had no choice but to follow the old man's instructions, summoning several crew members to follow him, and handing a handgun to the officer.

The old man arrived at the cabin, pushed the door open and went inside. The middle-aged man was calmly packing his luggage. Seeing several uniformed men behind the old man, his face immediately turned pale. The old man pointed at him and said to the sailors:

"Keep an eye on this man first!" Several sailors surged forward from left and right.

The middle-aged man was very cunning, not resisting, only asking them sternly: "What's going on!" The old man stared at him, saying:

"Friend, you should tell the truth. Where has that young man gone? We've come to you to find him!"

"How would I know? He just went up there," the middle-aged man continued to quibble.

The old man seemed very confident, directing the sailors to search the cabin, under the bed, in the slightly larger boxes, searching all suspicious places, but the young man was still nowhere to be found.

The old man pondered, examining the room, but there was no place large enough to hide a corpse. But suddenly, the old man caught sight of a neatly packed bedding roll on the luggage rack above the bed. He walked over and sniffed it, and a revolting, strange fragrance emanated from it. The old man understood. He hurriedly retreated to the doorway, triumphantly ordering the sailors to open the bedding roll, but he quickly turned his head away.

Hearing the old man's last words, the middle-aged man immediately convulsed, his legs giving way.

I imagine no one wants to see what's in that bedding roll? The outside is a burlap cover, wrapped in a blanket, and inside the blanket is a neatly laid out sheet of oil paper. But inside the oil paper, is a mud of flesh and blood... The old man's suspicion was correct, the young man was indeed still quietly lying in that room.

Why did the old man smell a strange fragrance from the bedding roll? I don't believe there could be such a cruelly meticulous murderer in this world, even in our cruel feudal society.

"Let Us All Weep Together" 221

— Xingzi

It wasn't by chance that I passed by the New World. Earth-shattering gongs and drums were ringing inside, and outside the door were colorful arches made of pine and cypress. I thought, today isn't Christmas, but, immediately, my thoughts turned back, knowing that this was related to the large advertisement in the newspaper saying "Let Us All Weep Together." Touching my heart, although it seemed a little sour, but, weeping, I couldn't manage a quick tear. I steeled myself and slipped through the crowd of "devout men and women" who had "come to weep together."

However, this slip made the sourness in my heart grow heavier. I slipped to the Sincere Company, and looking back, I even felt a little regret! I cursed myself for being a fool, but God is above, I certainly didn't curse myself for being a "cold-blooded animal."

I thought, this must be so lively! In this clamor of gongs and drums, there are "flowers," there are "stars," there are songs, there are dances, there are "patriotic" tears, there are "compassionate" tears, there are "tearful" smiles...

I thought, this must be so meaningful! Saving the country, saving people, and cultivating blessings, accumulating good deeds, and truly opening up a "heart of concern for the country!" Achieving five things with one action...

I also thought: this must be so romantic and delicate! After saving the country, in the spare time of saving people, "My 'flower,' come here," and present a beautiful floral crown! "My 'star,' come here" and dance a schottische, fragrant flesh, fragrant powder...

Thinking so much, I counted on my fingers: it's lively, it's meaningful, and it's romantic and delicate. Immediately, it felt like ants were crawling on my heart, itchy.

Until this moment, I was still regretting. I hated my tears for not rising to the occasion, I cursed myself for being a fool. But, God is above, I certainly didn't curse myself for being a "cold-blooded animal!"

Written to Unmarried Sisters 222

— Ms. Ziju

Dear Sisters:

You are swimming in sweet dreams, aren't you? Ideal futures are turning over in your minds, aren't they? But, time is dying away second by second, and real life will be revealed one scene after another in your life's history. When you discover that reality is far from ideal, you will be alarmed, annoyed, saddened, and grieved.

We can have idealized dreams forever, but at the same time, we have to welcome the arrival of real life. Reality is ordinary; no one can leave this ordinary life. Marriage is the first step from idealized dreams into real life. Before you embark on this stage, you must be prepared. First, I have to ask if you already have a lover? If you already have one, then you will take a further step to get married: but you must be prudent, are your partner's interests and habits the same as yours? This is the most important thing. When I say interests and habits, I generally mean daily life and academic research. Otherwise, if you are temporarily blinded by passion and unite, after the start of communal life, you will gradually drift in opposite directions. You want to go west, he wants to go east. In this China that still respects virginity, it's best not to divorce unless absolutely necessary, so you must be cautious from the beginning.

Second, the question of your two ages. Women age more easily. Men's sexual lives can extend to sixty or seventy, while women's end as early as forty or as late as fifty-three or four. Therefore, your partner must be older than you. It is of course not appropriate for a young woman to marry an old man, and it is even more inappropriate for an older sister to marry a younger brother. It is best if you are seven or eight years younger than him. Cohabitation is of course not entirely dependent on sex for its maintenance, but at least it occupies a chair in the entire life. In addition, if you are very strong and healthy, do not marry a sickly husband; if you are weak and sickly, it is best not to marry a fat and healthy person.

Third, in your passionate love, do not lose your rational judgment: A. You must not get married before you complete your studies. B. Love is best developed gradually, with more contact with each other, mutual recognition, and mutual understanding. It is better to become a couple from many years of friendship than to have a sudden, quick, love-at-first-sight union. C. You must consult with your close friends or parents and solicit their opinions. Those involved are confused, those watching are clear. They will definitely give you good advice.

Fourth, before you get married, you must ask yourself, do you have common sense about sexual life? Marriage is the beginning of sexual life. This is not a shameful or mysterious thing. You must study it early, at least read a book about sexual hygiene or sexual life. Many virgins, due to lack of this common sense, never get satisfactory pleasure and diseases follow. Isn't this very painful?

Fifth, it is naturally not permissible to embrace the supremacy of love, to sacrifice everything for love, until you have no self, no career, no standpoint, and become someone else's person; but if you are determined to play with the opposite sex, to provide for your sensory pleasure and satisfaction, playing with people often equals playing with yourself, especially in a male-centered society. You should shift your free time and the cleverness and talent to play with people to academic research and enthusiastic career development. This is the real new woman. The above are a few random thoughts. I don't know what the sisters think? I will discuss them with you another day.

Strange News of the Australian Aborigines (3) 223

— Weihan

The aborigines' concept of God is also very interesting. Generally speaking, God is an eternally immortal and extremely lofty being, who usually lives in the sky. He has a very large human posture, red skin, long hair that falls to his shoulders, and feet like those of an emu. (The emu is a giant bird native to Australia, resembling an ostrich.) Some gods even have feet like dogs and have many wives. The nature of God is very kind; they only govern the heavens, but do not interfere with earthly affairs. They do not create people, nor do they care about human affairs. However, legend says that they are very happy to take the souls of good people to heaven, and the aborigines firmly believe this. This concept of God varies from tribe to tribe. This is just a general concept.

Wall-Gazing Idle Talk - Ye Lingfeng 224

Two Red Lilies

There was a time when I was very obsessed with the works of Anatole France. I loved his gorgeous rhetoric, esoteric views, and the rich, pure scholarly atmosphere that permeated every book.

During such a time, on a sunny winter morning, holding his extravagant "Red Lily," I sat side by side with Lü on a park bench. The azure sky bathed in the warm sunlight, and I unknowingly betrayed my Anatole France. Although I held it in my hand, I treated his elaborate masterpiece as black decorations on white paper, not seeing a single word.

Looking at the silent Lü, her plump face, tight, small vermilion lips, and the two or three curls of hair hiding beside her ears, I couldn't help but feel a whim. I said, "Don't move, I'll draw a portrait of you."

The "Red Lily" in my hand happened to have a page of neat blank space. I pulled out a pen, and with an ambition comparable to that of the creator, I nimbly wrote down her face.

After finishing the drawing, I asked for a little rouge from her makeup case, dipped my finger in it, and lightly applied it to the cheeks of the person in the drawing.

I gave it back to her, and she smiled sweetly. After looking at it for a moment, she said to me:

"Give it to me. It's drawn too well. Keeping it with you will make me jealous. I don't feel at ease. Give it to me."

My clever mind has long known what is most precious in the world, so I tore off a page of this Red Lily without any reluctance. I know that this is like cooking a crane and burning a zither, but, cooking for a refined scholar and breaking for a confidant, Anatole France is also a discerning person. I know he will surely understand my actions.

With the falling flowers, one spring, the wind also took her away from my sight. For five years, the dust of the world has dimmed the impression she left in my heart. A luxurious "Red Lily" has also long lost its former glory, quietly standing in a corner of the bookshelf. Looking at this book on the shelf, gazing at its dim appearance, a deep regret arose in my heart. I have ended my life of luxury and have long been freed from the net, but it seems that it still carries a haggard lovesickness, yearning for that leaf that was torn off and scattered in the world.

December 16th

New Scientific Weapons 225

— Yi

Indeed, there are now some people who dislike war and curse it; but, on the other hand, in terms of firepower weaponry, in addition to tanks, armored vehicles, fighter planes, bombers, reconnaissance planes, airships, etc., which stand in the front line, toxic gases are also rapidly progressing, preparing to exert their maximum power. And wireless control (machines, electric cannons, death rays, etc.), which sprouted at the end of the Great War, if the war were to be extended by two or three years, then these kinds of weapons would inevitably have to be moved to the battlefield. However, since the Paris Peace Conference, what is the effect of these weapons? What are the results of the experiments? Countries have not mentioned much, as if there is no such thing. The reason for not mentioning it is that everyone's research on new weapons is particularly secretive, and everyone regards electrical weapons as precious treasures and is unwilling to reveal them easily.

Here, we can decisively say: electrical weapons! Are the most active machines in future wars.

First, let's talk about wireless control! Using radio waves and other radiation, arbitrarily controlling tanks, ships, and airplanes in the vicinity of the battlefield, without harming one's own soldiers, but being able to defeat the enemy, this is called wireless control. Major weapons on the future battlefield, such as explosive airplanes, can carry a large number of bombs and descend upon the enemy's camp, even launching a distant attack on the enemy's capital and major cities; or a ship full of gunpowder can sail like a ghost into the enemy's commercial and military ports and suddenly explode, thereby blockading the harbor. Warships without commanders attack each other with fierce artillery fire on the high seas, while the controllers of these ships are thousands of nautical miles away in a safe zone, drinking tea and smoking cigars while manipulating radio waves.

What is now called war always involves a final bayonet charge. Such things in future wars may become historical relics. Perhaps some people think that this kind of scientific progress is still years away from reappearing. However, facts tell us that wireless control has already had excellent results: I remember that at the end of the Great War in 1917, Germany used mines loaded on airplanes and remotely controlled them with radio to attack the enemy's naval base. Another example is that the U.S. Navy used wireless control to test the dropping of bombs on the battleship "Iowa" the year before last. Recently, when using the 22,000-ton battleship "Utah" as a target ship, wireless control was again tested. There was not a single person managing the battleship, but it was able to speed arbitrarily on the ocean. At present, it is only a live-fire exercise to avoid dangerous tests; but in the future, on land, at sea, and in the air, wireless control will occupy a very important position, that is without doubt.

"Go to class."

Zhang Yingkui's unhappy words.

He blushed and hurriedly followed Mr. Wang into the classroom.

(10)

"He's always taking leave."

"That's right, that fellow is very active. I don't know what he's up to."

Comments

After the Resumption of Relations 227

— Wu

Since the announcement of the resumption of relations between China and Russia, my friend said: "China is saved." Perhaps the degree of this "saving" does not necessarily mean that China can be lifted from the eighteenth level of hell to become the world's number one strong country, but the resumption of relations between China and Russia is indeed a happy event. For example, two good friends who suddenly fall out over a trivial matter are now reconciled again, and of course both parties have unspeakable joy in their hearts. Moreover, the fact that our compatriots are singing and dancing because of the resumption of relations is also a fact, as evidenced by the current newspapers. The Tianjin business community generally approves of the resumption of relations with Russia. After the Russian consul arrives in Tianjin, they will deliberate on purchasing Russian goods to replace enemy goods.

No problem, the resumption of relations between China and Russia naturally benefits our business friends greatly. Originally, our poor and weak country cannot avoid being supplied with foreign goods. If this is the case, if the source of goods is cheap, of course those doing business can make a few more profits. Then Russian goods are cheap, which is expected, because according to Russia's trade policy, its export of goods is not for the purpose of making money, but not without the idea of mutual communication: exporting products that cannot be consumed domestically to foreign countries, exchanging them for money, and then buying important industrial products that the country does not have or lacks. Therefore, what is sold to China can naturally be much cheaper than the goods of capitalist countries. In this way, of course, our business community can smile happily, with silver dollars and ingots rolling in.

As for saying that Russian goods are used to replace enemy goods, it is also naturally possible. And it sounds even better in name. Although selling enemy goods makes money, it always carries some risk and is also given the title of "奸商" [treacherous merchant]. Do you think that Russian calico is not enough to compete with enemy printed calico? So since it makes money and is "patriotic," and due to this moving appeal, more customers can be attracted, achieving several goals in one fell swoop, why not do it?

Therefore, everyone is happy about this resumption of relations, and the comrades in the Tianjin business community are even happier. Well then, the Emperor's grace is vast, and the whole world is celebrating together. And everyone says: "We are saved from now on."
