Science

The Function and Illuminating Apparatus of X-Rays 229

— Shen Yong

In the scientific world today, there are various names for light rays, such as infrared light (Infrared Light), ultraviolet light (Ultraviolet Light), etc. Since they are all a kind of light, why must so many names be given? Of course, there are differences between them. In fact, however, their wavelengths are slightly different.

The X-rays that we are going to talk about now, according to the research of scientists, have been proven in many ways to be the same as light, but just different in the light wave. The light wave of X-rays is particularly short, only one ten-thousandth of that of sunlight (SunRays). This is indeed a mysterious and mysterious light ray. People have used its power to do things that could not be done before and to understand the principles of the world that were not discovered before. Therefore, X-rays are really new products of civilized progress and scientific prosperity, and they are also a kind of power that helps the progress of world culture. Now, let me introduce the functions of X-rays in sections:

(1) The function for medicine 丨 The most common is that you can see broken bones, or bullets that have fallen into the body, and internal diseases such as tuberculosis can also be treated. Even the most dangerous internal carbuncle (Cancer) can be treated in the early stages using the R-rays or X-rays. At least it can be reduced somewhat. These are all cases where the disease has been contracted and treated with it. Apart from this, we can rely on this power to prevent diseases. That is, people without obvious or special problems can use X-ray photos to examine their bodies. If there are any shortcomings, they can first find ways to prevent or nourish themselves. From the above, how great is the contribution of X-rays to medicine?

(2) Function for industry 丨 Now machines have too much function for people's lives, but the more powerful the machine, the more careful you are, the consequences of the accident are directly proportional to its power. Therefore, if there are any problems with these metal castings, such as kerosene burning pots, airplane rotors, such as whether there are air holes, cracks, or sand inclusions, it is necessary to rely on the results of X-ray observation to avoid defects. There are also inspections of the quality of welding (Weld), the insect eyes and knots of wood, the inner diameter of measuring metal objects, and the investigation of the blockage of gasoline pipes, which also need to be seen with the help of X-rays. There is also a kind of asbestos that often looks similar but has different practical properties, and only X-rays can analyze it. In addition, gelatin, explosives, paraffin, cowhide, coal, and cement can all be used with X-rays to determine their quality.

Page 18

(3) Contribution to physics 丨 Relying on the power of X-rays, we can study the internal structure of matter, and understand the principles of atoms and molecules. Although a microscope (Microscope) can magnify matter thousands of times, the smallest unit of matter's structure can never be seen, and only X-rays can give us the final solution. The function of X-rays mentioned above has been briefly discussed. Now, I will briefly explain its device.

For the common manufacturing method, first take a glass tube and blow it into a spherical shape. The diameter of the glass ball is about six inches. At each end of the ball, connect a glass tube with a diameter of about one inch. A tungsten (Tungsten) electrode should be installed in the tube. One end is like a copper coin, which is the cathode; one end of the anode is plate-shaped, and the plane is inclined at forty-five degrees. After installation, evacuate the air in the tube completely and seal the tube mouth, then it is finished. When in use, connect an electric induction coil (Induction Coie) to the two electrodes. Electrons emitted from the cathode are called cathode rays (Cathode Rays). The speed of emission is very fast. When it encounters tungsten, it emits this mysterious X-ray, which cannot be seen by our naked eyes, but can penetrate various substances and the effect can be photographed.

Recently, a kind of X-ray tube called Coulidge tube has been invented by Dr. Coulidge of the United States. The method is to take a tungsten helix as the cathode and pass the current of a storage battery through it, just like an electric lamp. If the voltage of the battery is very high, it can emit very strong X-rays.

Respect and Cherish Written Paper 230

— Tianfang

丨Two Different Views丨

The office, fifteen minutes after lunch, is a place for free discussion. As usual, each person lights a cigarette and engages in discussions that contribute nothing to the people's livelihood, hoping to elicit a laugh. Conversations range from major national affairs to minor neighborhood matters, covering everything.

Today, after lunch, everyone sat down as usual, and just as they were about to start a verbal battle but hadn't found a topic, the office boy came to empty the wastepaper basket, and so the conversation started from there. Little Zhang said, "I really don't understand why people advocate 'respect and cherish written paper'? Once a newspaper or a page of an old book is discarded, its usefulness has already been lost. Is such wastepaper really worth respecting?"

"Not so," said Mr. Chen, whom we always call "Senior," and who usually doesn't participate in discussions. Suddenly, everyone perked up. He said, "Writing was created by the ancient sages and is a powerful tool for spreading culture; its contribution is great. Therefore, regardless of whether it is useful or not, it should be respected. If you see written paper on the road, you should pick it up and burn it, not trample on it." The old gentleman said very seriously.

"This is a traditional view, a strategy used by the 'scholar' class in the past to elevate their status. Let me ask, if you say that writing should be respected because it was created by the ancient sages and is a powerful tool for spreading culture, then what nation doesn't have its own writing, and what kind of writing doesn't spread culture? And why, sir, did you just use an English newspaper to wipe the table, but you respectfully placed a piece of wastepaper with Chinese characters into the wastepaper basket? Isn't this a contradiction? Therefore, 'respect and cherish written paper' is just a traditional view, a habit, and something that doesn't need to be respected now!" Little Li retorted layer by layer like a lawyer.

"I think written paper doesn't necessarily need to be respected, but wastepaper is worth cherishing, and it's a pity to burn it. Because paper mills can collect it and remake it!" Old Yang, true to his pragmatic nature, offered another opinion.

"Burning it is still the best," Senior replied simply to Old Yang. "Paper mills collect it and destroy the writing, which is terrible and sinful. Moreover, the ashes of written paper are also useful; when sailing and encountering wind, they can be poured into the water to suppress the wind!"

Old Yang said, "This is a 'myth,' and we are talking about 'human talk.' Utilizing waste is not a sinful thing!"

"You are all young people, only talking about utilization..."

Senior said silently, filled with disappointment, and went back to his seat to work.

Strange Events Discovered This Year 231

— Bai Hong

"Strange events happen every year, but this year is especially full of them!" A friend of mine said this as soon as he saw me. I hurriedly asked him what strange events he was talking about. He said, "Please sit down, please sit down! Let me tell you slowly..."

The first strange event is that a ghost appeared in the Xian'en Temple (?) in Yixing. Moreover, it is a young female ghost, weeping day and night, and interacting with heroic soldiers. This is a tragic and headless romantic case, possibly involving a monk in a lonely temple raping and murdering a solitary young girl. The strange thing is that the ghost can appeal to the heroic soldiers, and can cry, understand human intentions, and even obtain a blood-stained garment and skeletal remains, providing evidence for the case. Naturally, one cannot say that it is superstition or not. This case has already been sent to Nanjing for examination and is now being sent to Shanghai for investigation.

The second strange event is that a monster appeared in a certain place (forgive me for not remembering the place name). Its shape is like a sheep, and a certain young girl from a certain village was bewitched by it. Whenever the monster came, the young girl would climb onto the bed and make obscene remarks. Over time, she became emaciated and unrecognizable, having been ravaged by the monster. Later, this young girl was sent to the Qi family to be hidden away. Then, two sisters with a certain surname suffered the same ravaging. This strange event was reported in newspapers with detailed and convincing accounts, including names and surnames, indicating that it truly happened. Can you say that it is just nonsense like the stories of Qi Dong?

The third strange event is that Liang Zuoyou donated 30 million to save the country, but in the end, he didn't have a penny and was chased away by people. A young man who sells sesame cakes and fried dough sticks was able to travel to the capital, talk about national affairs with important figures in the National Government, and make shocking statements. Truly a strange person and a strange event.

The fourth strange event is that the Heavenly Emperor, Earthly Emperor, and Human Emperor appeared in Linyi County, Shandong Province, China. The Heavenly Emperor is Li Yuechuan, the Empress is Song Wangshi, and the Earthly Emperor is a tailor named Fu Baoqi. They planned to ascend the throne next March, fulfilling their imperial dream, proclaiming themselves as true Sons of Heaven, and selecting concubines and palace maids. It is said that the Heavenly Emperor had already appointed the Liu sisters, the fifth and sixth daughters of the county, as the Empresses of the East and West Palaces. Unfortunately, the emperor did not succeed, and now the Heavenly Emperor, Earthly Emperor, and Empress are all in prison. The Human Emperor is conveniently on the run. This is truly a strange event. In the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, three true Sons of Heaven actually appeared!

Now, the twenty-first year of the Republic of China is almost over, and this year can be considered to have had many strange events. Confucius said, "When a country is about to perish, there will surely be monsters!" Now that the Northeast has fallen and Tianjin and Peiping are in danger, if he is unfortunately proven right, that would be terrible, and we would become quasi-slaves of a fallen nation!"

My friend spoke eloquently, leaving me stunned and seeing only darkness before my eyes!

The Experience of Seeking Another Chance to Study, Editor: 232

Today, after reading Mr. Zhu's article "How to Get Another Chance to Study," I was immediately filled with endless feelings. This is truly a case of shared suffering! Currently, I am personally working hard to fight against reality. Although I don't know what the result will be, I might as well write about my difficult journey of studying for everyone's reference.

My studies were fraught with many setbacks from the beginning. In my childhood, I indulged in play, and it wasn't until after graduating from elementary school that I realized that studying was very interesting. Later, I don't know why, but I switched to a private school, reciting the Analects for less than half a year, "eating without tasting its flavor." Then, I transferred to an English school with no teaching methods, specializing day and night. During this process, life was monotonous and extremely boring. After two years, I resolved to transfer to a higher elementary school, and it wasn't until the age of sixteen that I was able to graduate. The suffering during this time was entirely due to the improper guidance of my parents, who had no fixed direction, leading me astray.

Due to family circumstances, I had no choice but to enter the business world, completely interrupting my passionate desire to study. However, I was able to become an apprentice in a warehouse of a company in Pudong, which, in terms of opportunity, was not bad. Outside of work, I also had quite a bit of leisure time. Of course! My thirst for knowledge, which I never forgot day and night, surged up like the tide.

I thought, "The opportunity to study again" has arrived! So I enrolled in a commercial English night school in the city. Knowing that I was striving to learn, I made rapid progress. After completing the course, I enrolled in a Chinese-English night school, from which I graduated the year before. Then, I consulted various books and engaged in self-study; but I encountered many questions that were very difficult to solve, even after consulting the dictionary. It was inconvenient to ask my former teachers. It wasn't until the autumn of this year that I was admitted to a certain college. Now? I feel that I am struggling to keep up with the course, especially the foreign professors, whose lectures I simply cannot understand. However, I am still humbly determined, ignoring everything except the tasks that need to be done, and working diligently day and night. I believe I will eventually find the light.

Yang Zongxia Offers Three Ways to Satisfy the Desire for Knowledge, Editor: 233

A young person who drops out of school halfway and enters the business world certainly feels very painful. To resolve this pain and satisfy his desire for knowledge is, of course, a very important matter. Now, I will express my opinions below for the reference of those who have dropped out of school.

(1) If an apprentice, trainee, or clerk has free time at night, they can join a night school to study.

(2) If the store's rules are that "clerks and apprentices are not allowed to go out at night," or if all free time is uncertain, then joining a correspondence school is more appropriate.

(3) If there is free time but economic problems arise, then the only option is to read more beneficial newspapers and books during daily life, or to communicate more with former classmates. Because those who are able to continue their studies will naturally know more places than you, and you can also ask them about things you don't understand.

Xi Hengxin

Regulations for the Sales Clerk Communication Column

(1) Purpose of Communication: The purpose of this column is to gather ideas, explain difficult problems, learn from each other, and enhance the happiness of life.

(2) Target Audience: The target audience of this column is limited to sales clerks and apprentices, and geographically limited to this city.

(3) Content of Communication: Anything related to personal daily life, such as:

(1) Occupation (2) Moral and academic cultivation (3) Entertainment and exercise (4) Marriage, as well as other issues related to the country and society, are all welcome. If the content of the problem is too profound and beyond the capacity of this column, it can also be referred to this newspaper's "Reader Advisor" for answers.

(4) Method of Submission

(1) The surname, age, native place, occupation, and detailed contact information must be written at the end of the letter; this information must be written again for subsequent letters.

(2) The writing style is not limited, but it should be concise and easy to understand, and it must be written clearly.

(3) Please write "Sales Clerk Communication Column, Supplement of Shen Bao Newspaper of this city" on the envelope. If a reply is required, please attach a two-cent stamp.

(4) Communicators must cut out the special stamp published by this column and paste it on the upper left corner of the letter. Submissions without the stamp will not be answered.

(5) Processing Method After Receiving Letters

(1) Any issues discussed that the newspaper believes have value in contributing to the public may be disclosed in the newspaper.

(2) To respect the opinions of the communicators, if the letter states that the author does not wish to disclose their name or requires a separate reply, it can also be done.

(3) If the communicator hopes to have the letter disclosed in the newspaper, but the length is too long to disclose the entire text, an abridged version will be published. Also, if the content of the problem is complex and requires careful study, which may delay the response or disclosure, please understand. (4) When there is a large volume of letters, they will be answered in the order in which they were received, and delays are to be expected.

Writing a Letter to a Friend's Wife (Continuation 10) 234

— Qin Shouou

Despite my usual ability to remain calm, I couldn't help but exclaim "Ah!"

"Haha! This is really a coincidence. Mr. Zhu, we haven't seen each other for almost three years!" She still smiled and talked as she used to.

I still remember when she was at Kouda, sitting high on the Queen's throne. Anyone who saw her couldn't help but praise, "How beautiful!" Even I, though I didn't worship her, couldn't deny her beauty. Now I see her again. Comparing her to you, one can't find where her beauty lies. At least you are a fairy; she is at most a demon!

"Ah! Miss Li! No, maybe you are now Madam Something, but we are old classmates," a humorous person, no matter when, even lying on the dissecting table in the hospital, can't help but say a few jokes. "No matter what Madam you are, I still have to call you Miss. Your Majesty the Queen! Is that right?"

She giggled, lasting a full four or five minutes.

Da Jing used to be infatuated with her because of the magic of this laugh. At that time, they were both top students in the law department. I, on the other hand, was studying economics; but because she was the Queen of the whole school, a Queen who was good at socializing, I often met her. And every time I saw her, I always saw Da Jing with her; he was like a loyal and filial subject, very respectfully following behind her high-heeled shoes.

The bachelor's thesis that Li Fang submitted upon graduation was also written by Da Jing. Little friend! Imagine, in a hot early summer, Da Jing writing two theses at the same time, not to mention how much brainpower was squeezed out, the stinky sweat that flowed must have been no less than twenty pounds! Originally, where love lies, even shedding blood, let alone sweat, is willing; what was distressing was that Miss Li was not moved by it!

Da Jing's infatuation with Li Fang, regardless of everything, was indeed a sensation throughout the school at that time. Da Jing was originally a bookworm who spent all day crouching in the library, and no one had ever seen him on the sports field, partly because he was too physically weak; but once Li Fang actually had the ability to encourage him to participate in the inter-class football game, making him wear a pair of nearsighted glasses with a depth of five or six hundred degrees, exposing a body that only showed bones and no flesh, mixed among many strong men of Yan and Zhao, and brave warriors of the South, desperately working hard. The result, of course, was a hundred jokes and physical disabilities; while Li Fang leaned in the arms of another man, laughing wildly for sixty minutes. For a woman to play with a man like this, one can't help but make men feel ashamed! But Da Jing enjoyed it and considered it an unparalleled honor.

Li Fang's father, it is said, had served as a military commander, and since he had been a military commander, he would naturally make money; since he knew how to make money, the family was naturally very wealthy; since the family was wealthy, Li Fang's expenses were naturally extravagant. However, this lady's spending was really too extravagant. Although the money the family gave her was not a small amount, she still felt that it was not enough; so Da Jing became her treasurer, inevitably bowing and scraping to provide her with his own money.

But Da Jing was not born into a wealthy family. Beautiful little pig, you probably already know that! The money he used to study at Kouda was supported by his mother selling the family's land. So, no matter how frugal and diligent he was himself, not daring to waste a penny, just socializing with this Queen was already too much to handle. One winter, he was only wearing a very thin camel hair robe, and his legs were playing the pipa in the classroom for more than a month; later, I secretly asked him, and I learned that his two leather robes had turned around in the pawnshop and were listed under the Queen's extra income account.

Construction Special

Summary of Conversations with Architect Wudak on Designing a Twenty-Two Story Building for the Four Banks 235

The twenty-two story building of the Four Banks Savings Society, currently under construction, is the tallest building in Shanghai. This publication believes that such a great project must have things worth studying for the construction industry, so the reporter and Mr. Sun Liyi, the architect of the Four Banks Construction Department, visited architect Wudak, the designer of the new building. He was kind enough to tell us the general situation, which we have recorded as follows:

Portrait of Architect Wudak

This Building is the Tallest Building Outside of the Americas

A site of the same size has a building of a certain size. As far as the new building of the Four Banks is concerned, its volume is 1.6 million cubic feet. If the entire area of the site, including the area currently occupied by Yunfei Automobile Company, is used to build the new building, then its average height would be 84 feet. However, the side facing the road has superior advantages in terms of location, traffic, air, light, and appearance. Therefore, it was decided not to include the area occupied by Yunfei. As a result, the height of the new building can be increased to 264 feet. As for the piles, they are 115 feet long, connected by 75-foot and 45-foot fir wood with steel hoops. In addition, 20 feet were excavated, for a total depth of 135 feet. Within this 20-foot excavation, a 5-foot deep reinforced concrete foundation was made to further strengthen the foundation. As for the mud excavated within the 20 feet, it weighed 11 million pounds. In other words, this 11 million pounds is the buoyancy used to calculate the moving load (Line Load) of 18 million pounds. Therefore, the two can be offset, so the piles only bear the fixed load (Dead Load). The value of the piles alone is comparable to that of an ordinary three-story building.

The new building weighs 33 million pounds. The entire framework is made of alloy brass steel, supplied by Siemens China. This steel material is produced by Wanne Lin Steel Factory, and it is extremely tough and excellent. As for the pressure generated by the wind force, it is about three times the pressure of the new building itself. Therefore, the wind force calculation of this building is one of its special features. The new building has very few walls. Even if there are any, they are made of unusually strong and lightweight bricks, carefully constructed. The new building adopts a three-dimensional style, so as to increase its height. In addition, Mr. Lindsgog and Mr. Zoepke of the United Steel Factory also provided a lot of assistance in the design of the new building.

Overview of the Four Banks Building 236

— Sun Liyi

The rise and fall of world industry and commerce is often measured by the number of buildings, and the growth and decline of buildings is directly proportional to the progress and decline of business. After the Great War, the rise of industry and commerce in the United States was fully reflected in the sudden increase in the number of buildings. The rapid advancement of its industrial technology reached its peak in 1928. After 1930, all industries stagnated, and the construction industry also showed signs of decline.

Since its establishment in the twelfth year of the Republic of China, the total savings of the Four Banks Savings Society has increased from 140,000 to more than 54 million in ten years, an increase of about 40 times. Its architecture has also changed from old three-story buildings to self-built seven-story buildings, and branch offices have been established everywhere, and self-built warehouses have been built. As for the recent plan, it will be in 1933, when the twenty-two story building will be offered to our ever-changing city of Shanghai, to serve the public, and to build a permanent symbol in East Asia. It is also sufficient to represent the success of the joint cooperation between this society and 100,000 depositors.

The new building is located between Jing'an Temple Road, Parker Road, and Baker Road, only a stone's throw from the city center and the Bund. It is especially convenient for transportation to the residential areas of the British and French concessions. It faces the vast racecourse, and there are entertainment venues and movie theaters nearby, which will be the center of Shanghai's nightlife in the future. It is located at the transportation hub of the city, and it is a necessary route for traffic to and from the north, south, east, and west districts. This building will definitely be the best choice for banks and hotels.

The building occupies a foundation of 12,400 square feet, with two parts, front and back. The front part is 22 stories, 264 feet from the street, and the back part is 15 stories, with a roof garden on top. The entire building uses 1,200 tons of lightweight I-beam material as the frame, and cement and sand as the walls, covered with face bricks. Reinforced concrete floor slabs and aerated concrete brick partitions are used. The entire building uses large glass steel windows. The front part is equipped with three high-speed elevators for passengers, and the back part is equipped with two 300-foot speed elevators for servants and for loading and unloading goods.

The situation of each floor is briefly described as follows:

(1) The Lowest Floor (15 feet below ground)

(A) The society's cash vault, with 1-inch steel bars and 12-inch reinforced concrete walls, and a 12-inch new-style safe door. There are two staircases, which are both strong and convenient. (B) The society's safety deposit box, for storing valuables for depositors, with half-inch steel plates on all sides. There are 4,000 safety deposit boxes of various sizes, two 16-inch safe doors, cork floors, and new-style reflective lights. Outside the vault, there are 16 small rooms for tenants to check their stored items, and there is air conditioning and heating equipment.

(C) Boiler room, with three 79-inch large boilers to supply all heating, hot water, and high pressure, and one small boiler for the kitchen.

(2) Bottom Floor (8 feet below ground)

Account book vault, sundries vault, and silver vault, hot water storage tank. The remaining space is the upper part of the safety deposit box and boiler room.

(3) First Floor

(A) Main entrance and passageway. The exterior of the main entrance is stone-built, facing south towards the racecourse. Inside the door is a 160-foot passageway that leads directly to the counter area, west to the manager's office and affiliated offices, and one door on the east leads to the hotel, and another door leads to the safety deposit box.

(B) Counter area, 19 feet high, occupying about 3,600 square feet of space, all decorated with marble. New-style reflective lights and various latest equipment are provided, and everything is available to facilitate depositors.

(C) The southeast corner of the gate is made of cobblestones, specially used as a reception room for hotels. The three high-speed elevators used in the counter area are all located here.

(4) Second floor, only one partition is used as the office for the director and deputy director, and the offices of various departments of the General Assembly.

(5) Third floor, hotel, dining room, and wine room, etc.

Page 22

It has many features. Facing the racecourse, the entire area of West Zanglu and Jing'an Temple Road is in view. Therefore, large glass doors and windows are used on all three sides, and the windows are filled with fresh flowers and trees. In spring and autumn, when the flowers and trees are lush, watching horse races on the upper floor is like being in a flower garden. As for the equipment of air conditioning and reflective lights, it is even more unnecessary.

(6) Fourth floor, the front part is the passenger lounge and smoking room. The back part is the large kitchen. The kitchen is divided into three floors, with various meat cold storage rooms, cooking rooms, and cake-making rooms.

Its layout and equipment are all rationalized, similar to large European and American hotels, and even better.

(7) From the fifth to the fourteenth floors, there are guest rooms, rooms of various sizes, and the equipment is all excellent, such as wireless broadcasting and personal bathrooms, which are more novel and exquisite than ordinary hotels in Shanghai.

(8) The fifteenth floor is the roof garden and the large wine room, dance floor, etc., 160 feet above the ground. Its wide location and fresh air will be the only summer resort in Shanghai.

(9) The sixteenth to twentieth floors are small residences with two or three rooms, about 200 feet above the street. It is quiet and spacious away from the city center, which should be no different from living in the mountains.

(10) The twenty-first floor is open to the public for viewing, and the beautiful scenery of Shanghai can be seen at a glance. With the help of telescopes, you can see Pudong, Wusong, Zhenru, and Longhua.

(11) The twenty-second floor is the observation post for the Shanghai Fire Brigade. Fires within ten miles of the concession can be detected at any time.

The project is only one-third complete, and it will be fully opened by this time next year, adding to the visual pleasure of the people of Shanghai.

Mr. Tao Jungui, from Guilin, Nantong, has been operating the Fook Kee Construction Factory since its establishment. Based on his experience and strength, his construction achievements are remarkable. In recent years, he has devoted himself to this field, and many major projects in various outports have been undertaken by him, achieving remarkable results and a soaring reputation. He is a standout talent in the construction industry.

Mr. Jin Fulin, from Wuxian, is a rare talent in construction. He is extremely experienced in factory organization and factory management, and his knowledge is particularly rich. Since he has been in charge of the 22-story building project of the Four Banks Savings Society, the management and organization have been well-organized. The rapid progress of the building project shows this.

A photograph of the 20-story building of the Four Banks Savings Society taken when the 13th floor was under construction.

A Brief History of the Four Banks Savings Society 237

On January 24th, 1923, representatives from the Yien Yieh, Kincheng, China & South Sea, and Continental Banks met in Beiping and resolved to establish the Four Banks Savings Society under the Joint Business Office. They agreed on the regulations and articles of association and appointed Mr. Zhou Zuomin, General Manager of Kincheng Bank, Mr. Hu Yun, General Manager of China & South Sea Bank, Mr. Tan Lisun, General Manager of Continental Bank, and Mr. Wu Dingchang, General Manager of Yien Yieh Bank, as executive committee members. Mr. Wu Dingchang was elected as chairman, responsible for all affairs of the society. In February 1926, Mr. Qian Yongming was appointed as vice-chairman. Currently, there are Four Banks Savings Societies in Shanghai, Tianjin, and Hankou, and branches in Nanjing, Beiping, and other places, specializing in accepting various types of savings, including fixed-term, long-term, installment, and current deposits. Fixed-term deposits start from a minimum of twenty-five yuan, with a maturity of two years. Long-term deposits also start from a minimum of twenty-five yuan, with options of five or ten years. Five-year deposits accrue compound interest annually. Ten-year deposits accrue compound interest semi-annually. Installment deposits start from a minimum of one yuan per month, with a maturity of twenty-five months. All three types are guaranteed by the society with an annual interest rate of seven percent, and dividends are distributed within the term. Current deposits are divided into two types, A and B. Type A has an annual interest rate of four percent, and Type B has an annual interest rate of three percent, both of which are also eligible for dividends. Since the society's establishment in June 1923, the total amount of savings has increased from over one million four hundred and thirty thousand yuan (end of 1923) to over fifty-two million eight hundred and twenty thousand yuan (end of 1931). The highest total interest and dividend income received by depositors in previous years reached 11.7%, and the lowest was above 9.5%. The society's operations strictly comply with the regulations for savings banks, prioritizing stability, while the organization has a cooperative nature. All depositors are members, and dividends are distributed equally. The abridged accounts are checked and published by accountants and announced to members, ensuring complete transparency. The society's articles of association were submitted to the government for approval on March 14, 1923, and were approved by the Ministry of Finance of the National Government on August 27, 1931.

Implementation of Architectural Engineering Education in Three Major American Universities 238

Translated and narrated by Yuan Xianghua of the Shanghai Architectural Association

The advancement of modern science has made it impossible for those engaged in architecture to rely solely on practical experience, as they did in the past. Today, they must possess versatile talents to cope with the ever-evolving architectural industry. It goes without saying that architects must understand the process or steps involved in creating good architecture and should pay close attention to structural design. Structural planning is the central issue in creating good architecture, and neglecting it will inevitably lead to failure. Other aspects, such as construction management, material procurement, and miscellaneous tasks, all require skilled talent to handle. However, architects who possess the above qualities are rare, yet there is a large demand for them today.

A young person who wants to acquire practical architectural knowledge can learn from the factory floor through careful observation and diligent self-study. After a considerable period, they may be able to handle certain tasks with ease. However, architectural design and engineering management cannot be effectively learned through self-study alone and require guidance to grasp the essentials. However, architects, as chief engineers, are often too busy managing their own affairs to provide guidance to young apprentices. This is a real difficulty, and they cannot be blamed for it. Even with proper guidance on architectural design and engineering management, apprentices' knowledge is limited to their own industry or factory and rarely have the opportunity to develop new ideas or make connections between different fields. Therefore, a young person can easily acquire practical architectural knowledge in the workplace, but architectural theory cannot be obtained from the factory floor. However, relying solely on experience without emphasizing theory will lead to the drawback of "knowing what but not why." Therefore, success as an architect is difficult.

The development of the American architectural industry has reached its peak today. People enjoy the utmost happiness in living, which is due to the abundance of national economic power. However, the popularization of architectural knowledge among the general public is also a major reason for the rapid development of the domestic architectural industry. The government actively cultivates architectural talent to meet future needs, and private individuals or construction companies contribute funds to establish scholarships or lectureships at various universities to encourage young students to pursue architecture. The most notable example is the Thompson Starret Foundation, established by Louis J. Horowitz and Herwilz, which donated to the Massachusetts Institute of Technology, Yale University, and Union College for the establishment of architectural programs. In addition to the above foundation, the Horowitz couple also established scholarships to be awarded to outstanding graduates of the three universities who wish to pursue architecture and undergo designated internships at Thompson Starret Co. in New York. For clarity, the implementation of architectural engineering education at the three universities is summarized below for reference.

Stone Masonry Design (One of the Exercises for Students at the Massachusetts Institute of Technology) 239

1. Massachusetts Institute of Technology

The Massachusetts Institute of Technology is one of the most famous universities of science and engineering in the United States. The Department of Architecture is a combination of the seventeen sciences and engineering disciplines in the school. This department became an independent college in 1926, at which time there were only seventeen students, but it has been extremely developed to this day. The person in charge is Professor Ross F. Tucker. The duration of study is four years. All general disciplines relating to architecture are fully equipped. Students receive basic training in various disciplines in the first year. From the second year, they make on-site investigations of residential buildings. In the third year, they engage in the construction of industrial factory buildings. The first step is the simple

pile foundation design (Practice II for students at the Massachusetts Institute of Technology)

factory building construction of brick, stone, and wood. Then they proceed to the construction of cement. In the fourth year, they advance to the construction of steel-framed commercial buildings. After the professor lectures to a certain stage, he distributes the lecture outline to the students, instructing each student to prepare a report within one week using his own opinions and return it to the professor. After evaluation, it is returned again. This method is thoroughly implemented throughout the duration of study and is never interrupted. Therefore, when each student graduates, he can collect past reports and compile them into a volume as an excellent permanent reference material. The implementation of this teaching method is to cultivate students' ability to make automatic inventions and sound judgments or appreciation, thereby preventing past teaching materials from being forgotten and permanently engraved in their minds. In addition, oral and written examinations are also held on time. The scope of the examination includes ancient and modern architecture, so students must have a considerable understanding and image of modern and past architecture. Graduates receive a bachelor's degree and can also obtain the above-mentioned Horowitz Scholarship.

The university pays special attention to the four points of architectural materials: 1. source, 2. quality, 3. use, 4. procurement. This is also what we should pay attention to. The difference between the Department of Architecture and other engineering departments may also be based on this. Graduates of general architecture or engineering departments often neglect the point of architectural materials and do not have a special study. This is a great obstacle to their future development. It is important to know that architectural materials are like the skeleton of the human body and are the element that forms the entire building. Sometimes, after these graduates have entered the architectural industry or other businesses related to architecture, what they can work hard on or pay attention to is only the design or implementation of the project. As for substantive issues (architectural materials), as a result of neglecting them in student days, they must now work hard again and spend a considerable amount of time to study and investigate them before they can understand one or two of the above four points. In addition, the university's teaching purpose is also to cultivate people with quick thinking and swift action. Once an architectural difficulty arises, a decision should be made immediately and there can be no hesitation. And an architect is in a chaotic environment, and there is no time to hesitate. At that time, the steps or process of construction must be clear in mind, and there must be the ability to decide and judge on the construction instructions or the inspection of the structure. At this time, it is naturally impossible to carry reference books for on-site comparison. The knowledge of an architect must always be applied and there can be no interruption. Therefore, the university's education method is more important than "learning for use!"

2. Yale University

The Department of Architecture at Yale University is affiliated with the Sheld Scientific School of Yale Uni. The distribution of courses for each academic year is outlined below:

1. All courses in the first semester of the first year of university are similar to those of engineering in other universities. Such as: English, history, chemistry, mathematics, engineering drawing, etc. If all the subjects in the first year can pass, there will be no difficulty in advancing to the second year.

2. All courses in the second semester of the second year of university

are still basic subjects, in preparation for further studies next year. They include: physics, engineering mechanics, mathematics, engineering drawing, and English, etc.

3. From the third year to the third academic year, all courses begin to differ from those of the engineering department. In the first semester, considerable attention is still paid to physics, etc., and structural planning occupies a very important position in all disciplines. An overview of economics and an introduction to architecture are required courses. The principles of architecture, which are devoted to architectural materials, architectural comparison, standard design, etc., are also required in the second semester.

One of the Extracurricular Activities of Yale University Students 240

4. The disciplines from the fourth year to the fourth academic year tend towards practice, such as steel-framed cement construction, etc., and are given great attention. At this time, students are engaged in the design and implementation of architecture and the preparation of working drawings. In order to facilitate business after graduation, considerable attention is also paid to commercial subjects. In the first semester, the principles of accounting are taught, and in the second semester, there are engineering management contract research instruction research, etc. Such as project valuation, cost analysis, etc., are all given attention, so that scholars can have a good understanding of modern architectural science both theoretically and practically.

In addition, Yale University students attach great importance to summer work. There are three summer vacations during the four-year study period, each lasting four weeks. Architecture students use this time to practice abroad. The first summer (that is, the summer vacation between the first and second academic years, and so on.) is devoted to plane surveying. The second summer vacation advances to topographic surveying Topographic Sutveying The third summer vacation is led by a professor to visit

A photograph of the construction of the Rongjin Grand Theater, undertaken by Zhushengji Construction Factory

and inspection, the scope of which includes construction factories, architectural firms, material testing laboratories, and building material manufacturing factories, so that students can understand the organization of the entire architectural industry and its activities.

The implementation of various disciplines in the above academic years is still a kind of mechanical training. In addition, the school authorities are working hard to cultivate students' ability to have a broad perspective, so as not to be confined to one corner, so as to avoid the ridicule of sitting in a well and watching the sky. Students should pay attention to the disciplines of architecture, and it goes without saying that they should also have considerable research and cultivation in languages, aesthetics, and other aspects: and they should carefully consider the importance of their own position and the preparation for employment after graduation.

3. Union College 241

The Architectural Engineering Department of this university was first established with a donation from the Thompson Foundation. The duration of study is four years. In the first and second academic years, general architectural disciplines such as drawing, surveying, mathematics, and English are taught. In the third academic year, mechanics, economics, railway construction, hydraulics, and other disciplines directly related to architecture are taught. From the previous year, two courses of architectural materials and architectural form have been added. Students practice one of the drawings

Page 23

Part of the actual valuation, sometimes or engaged in the design of the renovation of existing buildings. When there is time after class, they practice the use of machinery, the installation of full lead pipes in houses, and the design of electrical engineering. In addition, pile foundations and skeletons are given great attention.

Among the courses offered at Union College, the structure course, regardless of theory or practice, is given more importance than others. In addition, great attention is also paid to economics, accounting, and corporation finance. It is assumed that when students go out to work, they will not have any regrets about financial management.

4. Other

In addition to the Thompson Foundation donating to the Architectural Engineering Departments of the three universities mentioned above, the Horowitz couple also donated considerable funds to Carnegie Institute Technogy to cultivate architectural talent. The person in charge is Professor Clifford G. Dunnejis. In the course offered, attention is paid to both the theory and practice of architectural engineering. The purpose of this university to cultivate talent is to cultivate students' ability to be independent implementers. Courses such as mathematics, physics, chemistry, mechanics, structural principles, as well as experiments in carpentry, brickwork, electrical work, and mechanical engineering are held on time, so that students do not have the disadvantage of disregarding experiments. Surveying is a required course. During the summer vacation between the second and third academic years, students must go out to practice. In addition, each student also visits the architectural projects that are in progress outside of class to supplement the lack of teaching materials with on-site observation, thereby developing new ideas and connecting them on their own.

Public Entertainment Buildings丨Elements of Building a Perfect City丨 242

— Zong Wen

Now, the general public in society pays too little attention to entertainment! And what they call entertainment is just some improper things… such as gambling and playing mahjong, just to pass the precious time. How dangerous this is! The harm is indeed not shallow! This is also one of the reasons why our China is weak. In Yeping's article "Amateur Entertainment and Playing Mahjong" in the second issue of the amateur weekly of this newspaper, the harm of this kind of improper entertainment has been said very thoroughly! But why do people generally neglect proper entertainment instead? The reason is that there are too few public entertainment buildings in the city; even if there are, they are just some private ones, so they cannot be universal to the general public. Therefore, because of this, the general public in the city will not pay attention to it. Therefore, if we want to make people in society abandon improper entertainment, we must start from building more public entertainment buildings in the city… But how should we design public entertainment buildings? This is what I want to talk about now. Speaking of public entertainment buildings, there are of course many kinds… such as gardens, sports fields, lawns, theaters… etc. Because these buildings

sufficient to make people interested, promote the spirit, make people healthy, and can cultivate the general aesthetic psychology… of course, its benefits are many! But look at our old China, there are too few public entertainment buildings of this kind! Even in Shanghai, which is prosperous in the country, except for the general private entertainment buildings, public entertainment buildings are really unique! This is really pitiful! Look at the countries in Europe and the United States, which attach great importance to the happy undertakings of the people. In the large and small cities, at the crossroads, there are always several squares of lawns and parks built for pedestrians to rest; (Shanghai only has the Bund area, but it is only a decoration) and various public games are set up, such as dance halls, parks, swimming pools, etc. Of course, this adds a lot of color to the city scenery! It can be called a "beautiful city." Because of this, it is enough to cultivate a strong nation, create various undertakings, and the country is therefore strong. From this, we know that the facilities of public entertainment buildings are also an element in building a perfect city, and this is not enough to show the beauty of the city. Therefore, in urban planning, a plan for public entertainment construction is also indispensable. Looking at China, because there are too few buildings of this kind… therefore, the general people have no proper entertainment to pass the time, and the spirit is therefore trapped, resulting in the pain of life. It is important to know that the spirit is the living element of life; if there is one, there is nothing that cannot be done… if there is none, there is nothing that can be done; this is the only major reason for the weakness of the Chinese people. The importance of public entertainment buildings has been described in general above; now let's talk about the facilities of public entertainment buildings.

First, let's talk about parks. According to parks, they can be divided into two types… 1. Natural parks outside the city. 2. Parks in the city. The natural park outside the city is formed by decorating the places with trees or mountains and rivers that are about two or three miles away from the city. This is created by using natural scenery. This kind of park only needs to buy several mountains and forests, and then build several roads leading to the city, so the cost is relatively saved. However, the construction of this type of park must be close to the city… If there is no such natural scenery around the city, then, of course, this type of park is not suitable, and the second type of park in the city must be built. …As Shanghai is of course suitable for the second type, because there is no such natural original scenery nearby…

Parks in the city are completely built artificially. They must meet the conditions of art in order to make tourists interested; however, these parks in the city can be divided into two categories… (A) Man-made large lawn. Various trees are planted around, and遊椅 are set up to provide tourists with leisure and pleasure; and exotic flowers and plants are planted in it to arouse the curiosity of those who pass the time and create aesthetic ideas. This kind of small park should be built in prosperous trading areas, and the more the better. (For example, the Hubin Park on the side of West Lake in Hangzhou is a very good example). (B) Man-made parks in the city. This kind of park is larger than the lawn park. Flowers, trees, and seats are of course necessary; and there are rockeries, pavilions, and small lakes in it. In addition, various public entertainment buildings such as tennis, football fields, swimming pools, dance halls, small golf courses, and various

A photograph of the cork planted by the New Silk Forest Yong'an Forest Company fifteen years later. The trunk is five feet eight inches in circumference and about seventy-five feet high, which is beneficial to the display of citizens. (For example, the Confucius Temple Park in Shanghai and various parks in the concession are several good examples). At least two of this kind of park must be built in each city. And it is especially suitable to promote in the inland, and more should be established. Because the land in the inland is of course cheaper than the city, and there are more hard-working compatriots and farmers in the inland, and the knowledge is low, so it is more necessary to promote high-level entertainment to adjust the boring and tasteless life of the general public. This is a very important thing, which has a great impact on the future of the country! How can we ignore it?

Game fields and theaters are also one of the public entertainment buildings, but one is of a business nature, and the other is a private building, so there is no need for the public to build it, but only to guide and guide it. But when we plan the city, we should divide the land for private buildings so as not to confuse it with other boundaries. For example, there should be no theaters in the factory area. In the commercial area, more public entertainment places such as theaters can be set up to help the development of business. In the residential area, more theaters should also be set up to provide residents with proper entertainment. These are what we must pay attention to in the construction of city planning.

In addition, the construction of public sports fields, gyms, etc. is also indispensable; whether it is a city, town, township, or village, they must be established. Because this is the center of people's sports and an indispensable tool for entertainment! According to the school sports fields in Europe and the United States, people and children are allowed to enter freely to exercise, but our China is indeed the opposite, so the schools are inevitably aristocratic, because people cannot easily enter to exercise! But I sincerely hope that the school authorities will be aware of this and freely open the playground to benefit the citizens. Otherwise, more public sports fields should be set up in the city, no matter how big or small, but always in proportion to the number of people, children, women, and others in the city, and according to this distribution, each should be built separately; this is of great importance to the health of the citizens, and how can we ignore it!

In short, the facilities and methods of public entertainment buildings must meet the following five conditions!

1. The facilities for public entertainment must be perfect, especially paying special attention to children and women.

2. The address must be located in the central location of the city, and the transportation should be especially convenient.

3. Do not take money丨Even if you take money, you should take the minimum fee.

4. It must meet the needs of the masses, but it must not cater to the low-level evil psychology of society.

5. Hire appropriate personnel to guide and supervise at any time.

Build it! Let us strive to build public entertainment buildings!

General Development of Forest Industries in New Zealand 243

Overview of New Zealand Yong'an Forest Company 244

New Zealand is the world's most productive pine-producing area. The growth rate of softwood trees there is about four or five times that of those produced in Canada or Europe. For example, the Pinuslnsignis pine tree can be harvested in only ten to fourteen years for the production of wood pulp, and new trees can be planted the following year after harvesting. The organization of New Zealand Yong'an Forest Company is to make full use of this natural resort to seek the full development of the forest industry. In 1924, the company opened up 53,805 acres of land in a superior location with convenient transportation, and its afforestation area was 9,733 acres. By 1926, it had increased to 449 cais and two acres. As of today, its planting area, including the 6,000 acres to be planted, has reached a total of 144,600 acres, and no less than 100 million trees have been planted. It is estimated that it can be harvested within four years, so the abundance of its profits can be imagined. The company has complete equipment and a magnificent scale, and its future development is truly immeasurable. It is reported that the company welcomes investment from all walks of life to share the profits in order to actively expand.

A photograph of the softwood planted by New Zealand Yong'an Forest Company after six and a half years 245

Bridge Construction and Falsework 246

— Erming

The construction method of a bridge on a bridge site can vary depending on the circumstances of the bridge and local convenience, and can be divided into two types: using falsework and not using falsework.

For ordinary steel frame bridge construction, if falsework can be erected locally, it is advisable to use falsework. For stone arch bridges and three-in-one soil arch bridges that require continuous supports, falsework must also be erected. Whether or not to erect falsework depends on whether piles can be driven into the riverbed, whether navigation is obstructed, whether there are difficulties during flood season, whether the river is very deep, and whether there are wooden rafts and ice floes drifting on the river surface.

Ordinary single-track steel frame bridge construction is suitable for falsework. Each frame consists of four wooden piles. One frame is used under each connection point of the frame beam bridge, and several frames are used between the connection points. The width of the frame must be such that, outside the position of the steel bridge frame beam on both sides, steel rails can still be installed, one on each side, for the use of cranes traveling on them. The crane is an inverted U-shaped frame that can lift various parts of the bridge, travel on the two rails, and place them in appropriate locations. This type of crane is very suitable for bridges with spans of 250 feet or more. For shorter bridges, mobile cranes can be dispensed with and internal traveling cranes can be used. As for the order of constructing steel frame bridges, the rail-bearing beams and transverse dyes are usually installed first, followed by the two main frames. However, in order to avoid river flooding and the collapse of falsework, and to complete the main frame beams in a relatively short time, the above order can be changed. The construction of falsework required for stone arch bridges or three-in-one soil arch bridges is more important and difficult than that for ordinary frame beam bridges. Firstly, arch-shaped frames are more difficult to make; secondly, arch bridges are subject to heavy loads, unlike frame beam bridges where the load is concentrated at the connection points. Therefore, arch bridge falsework must have continuous support, and special care must be taken when removing the falsework upon completion, ensuring that each part slowly detaches simultaneously, so that each part of the bridge receives pressure at the same time.

Method of Not Using Falsework If the river conditions do not allow for the construction of falsework, the bridge body can be loaded onto several ships elsewhere, towed to the bridge site, and then moved onto the piers. Although this may obstruct traffic for some time, it is a simple solution from the perspective of bridge construction.

If the river does not allow for falsework and it is inconvenient to move ships, then the cantilever method is the simplest construction method. This method involves building from both banks, gradually extending towards the center, and then joining the two halves together when they meet. However, even if it is not a cantilever bridge, but the cantilever method is used for construction, the stress of each part of the bridge during construction must be calculated separately. Some of the stresses may be opposite and cancel each other out from the original stress, while others may be the same and merge together. In this case, the materials must be increased appropriately. This is the uneconomical aspect of the cantilever method, but due to its simplicity, in addition to cantilever bridges themselves, other ordinary bridges and arch bridges are also often built using this method.

The method of not using falsework can also be mixed and used in conjunction with the falsework method. For example, for a long bridge with several spans, the falsework method can be used where possible, and the cantilever method can be used where appropriate, depending on the local conditions.

The construction of ordinary slab bridges generally does not require falsework; only cranes are needed to lift them from one bank and place them in the appropriate position.

The construction of bridges requires skilled workers and good tools in order to be fast and cost-effective. Which of the above construction methods is applicable sometimes depends on the availability of these skilled workers and good tools. If these two conveniences are lacking, it will be very costly to operate.
